More than thirty pieces of clothing, including men's and women's clothes, fur robes, and cheongsams, were found in the rice husker, along with an accomplice, Ding Xigen. They were both handed over to the district corps headquarters and then to the county on the 26th. When they reached the Sanjia Li area, Guo Chunbao tried to escape and was shot and killed by [Ding]. The county committee sent someone to the village today to inspect the scene. After Ding Xigen was handed over to the county, he was interrogated by Magistrate Li. Ding admitted that his father had gone to rob and that he had not gone himself. He was ordered to be detained.

Conflict Between Civilians and Police During a Search for Red Pills: Magistrate Li received a letter from a certain person in Shanghai reporting that Shen Hanquan's family in Caojia Lane, Hebei, Changjing Township, was selling red pills. Magistrate Li immediately ordered Ma Huaizhong, the captain of the Fourth Police Squad, to secretly arrest him in the village. After Ma arrived in the village, he sent seven plainclothes officers to Shen's house. Because many family members had gone to the Qi family for a wedding feast, neighbors claimed that Shen did not sell red pills. Ma went to search the home of Shen Hanquan's younger brother, Hanfeng (a vegetable vendor). At that time, for unknown reasons, he stirred up the villagers, causing a conflict, resulting in beatings. They were crowded into the office and surrounded, but Assistant Bao Hansheng stopped them and they were dispersed. They reported to the county and will handle the matter again.

Zhenjiang 78

False Report of Bandit Situation Results in Detention and Transfer to the Province: Zhou Shujiang, the captain of the Shuyang County Police Brigade, and Li [Feng], the deputy captain, made a false report of a bandit situation, resulting in the loss of an opportunity. This was discovered by Director Zhang of the Pacification Bureau, who escorted them to Yangzhou. After questioning them, he dispatched personnel to Zhenjiang to transfer them to the provincial government for handling. After being interrogated by Chairman Ye, he stated that the case concerned a criminal matter and immediately sent a letter to the Zhenjiang Court for investigation. He also dispatched a team to escort Zhou and Li to the court. The Prosecutor's Office opened a court investigation, and after much deliberation, ordered their detention pending investigation and handling.

Yangzhong 79

Director of Education Bureau Investigates New Account Books: In Yangzhong County, during the tenure of the former Director of Education, Wang Huankun, the income and expenditure of education funds were never made public. When the education surcharges and school rent were collected in January, the principals of the primary schools had not yet received their salaries. Therefore, on the day Wang left office, Liu Yulin and other primary school principals petitioned the county government to withhold the settlement. Fortunately, the county government only approved "to be reviewed after the new director investigates the account books."

Therefore, Wang was able to leave Yangzhong peacefully. In recent days, the new director, Fan Xuezhen, has been investigating Wang's previous account books. It is heard that one item of bureau expenses has exceeded the budget by more than one time. The director's travel expenses are always opened for thirty or forty yuan each time, and the office expenses paid monthly by Wang, who also served as the head of the social education section, were twenty-four yuan. There are many other irregularities in various other items as well. Yesterday, the principal of a certain fourth primary school came to the bureau to collect the expenses for December. According to the handover documents, it had already been paid and there were receipts. In fact, on the income side, 500 yuan had been received from the county government on February 8th. By the time of the handover on the 12th, no school had been paid, and the account books handed over showed that the former director still owed more than one hundred yuan. There are many doubts, which cannot be exhausted. It is now heard that Director Fan has reported the results of the investigation to the county government.

Yangzhou 80

Overview of Yangzhou Money Shops Reopening: It is customary for the money industry in Yangzhou to reopen on the fifth day of the first lunar month after the lunar calendar. Due to the relocation of the Yunsup and the depletion of funds, after the overall settlement, the money shops were unable to recover the money released, amounting to a huge amount of 1.2 million yuan, which caused them all to wait and see. Only today (the 26th), Hengda, Hengchang, Shenda, Juda, Jiuyu, Huichangyong, Dongyu, Chunhe, Qian [ ], Runchang, Yongyuan, Baoxing, Lichang, Dechun, [ ]yu, Hongda, Yonglong, Lifeng, [ ]tong, Qingda, Shengyuan, Yuanhe, and the newly opened Yisheng (changed from Jiufeng) and Yuanchang reopened, totaling twenty-four. Hengxingyuan, [ ]da, Ruitai, Ruifeng, Yifeng, Qinglong, Yihe, Shengchang, and Dechunrun nine shops have actually ceased operations. In addition, the situation of shops such as Yida is uncertain.

Execution by Firing Squad of Pirate Convicted of Robbery: Wang Yunqing, the convict who robbed the Fujian Company's Fengyu steamboat, was previously arrested in Zhenjiang by the Public Security Bureau's anti-crime squad. A Browning pistol and several pieces of stolen clothing were seized. The case was transferred by the Public Security Bureau to the Pacification Director's Office for handling. Li, the director of the military law office, interrogated the convict and, in accordance with Article 1, Item 13 of the Law on Punishing Bandits, had the convict tied up and escorted to the execution ground at the vagrant reformation center at 10:00 a.m. on the 26th for execution by firing squad.

Ningbo 81

The Executive Committee of the Yin County Party Department Has Been Selected: After the third executive committee of the Yin County Party Department was re-elected at the fourth county-wide representative meeting on the 7th of this month, the fifteen candidates elected, including Wu Wangji, were submitted to the Provincial Party Department for approval. It is now known that the Provincial Executive Committee approved the selection of Wu Wangji, Chen Boang, Zhang Xianlu, Lin Jianzhong, and Shi Shuyao as the third executive committee of the Yin County Party Department. The third supervisory committee of the Yin County Party Department must be approved after a meeting of the Provincial Supervisory Committee before it can be selected.

The Theft Case in Sujiayuan: Sujiayuan, located about ten li outside the south gate of Yuyao, is inhabited by Han Yunmen, who is over seventy years old and blind. He used to do business outside and had some savings. Suddenly, at 12:00 p.m. the other day, seven bandits broke down the door and stole jewelry and silver dollars, worth about four to five hundred yuan.

Before leaving, the bandits comforted Han Yunmen, who was sleeping in bed, before leaving leisurely towards the Nanmiao area.

Xiaoshan 82

Early Opening of Money Shops: There are six money shops in Xiaoshan County: Tongyu, Dehe, Shengda, Hengyuan, Fuyu, and Renyuan. After this overall settlement, Xu Renyuan suspended the release of loans outside of debt collection last year, while the others made profits ranging from two to three thousand yuan. Shengda and Dehe had the highest profits. It is scheduled to open on the 25th. In addition, Baochang Zhuang, a new store, was established and opened on the 20th.

Ordered to Investigate and Return the Construction Funds: The Xiaoshan County Government received an order from the Department of Construction yesterday instructing the county magistrate, together with the director of the Finance Bureau, to investigate and return the construction funds. The original order stated: 1. According to the report submitted by Gao Dezhong, director of the county Finance Bureau, the construction funds have been misappropriated by previous administrations and no longer exist, making it impossible to pay them off. We pray for a review and request the county to be exempted from paying. 2. The local tax revenues are specifically designated for certain purposes, and the income and expenditure must be appropriate. An annual budget is prepared as a basis. Even if there is a temporary transfer due to insufficient income, it should be collected and returned within this item to clear the accounts. The county's [ ] donation is a special fund for construction. It is said that it has been misappropriated by previous administrations. What specific purposes were they misappropriated for? Are there any outstanding debts that have not been collected to offset the debt? The director of the bureau is responsible for the overall management of finance. The county magistrate and the director of the bureau must investigate, clear, and return the funds as soon as possible.

The County Chamber of Commerce Elects Executive and Supervisory Committee Members: The Xiaoshan County Chamber of Commerce convened a general meeting of members of various industries at 1:00 p.m. on February 24th to elect executive and supervisory committee members and establish a formal chamber of commerce. A total of 135 member representatives attended. As a result, Zhu Jialin, Zhang Wangyun, Bo Bingjiong, Chen Xiangfan, and fifteen others were elected as executive committee members, and Chen Xiaobing, Zhu Zhaolin, Yu Lichuan, and seven others were elected as supervisory committee members. Zhu Jialin and Chen Nianzu were mutually elected as standing committee members, with Chen Nianzu as chairman.

The Business Tax Director Establishes an Office to Handle Affairs: Si Lie, the director of the Xiaoshan County Business Tax Collection Bureau, arrived in Xiaoshan on the 24th and went to the County Government Finance Bureau and the Chamber of Commerce to discuss all matters. It is now scheduled to begin collecting taxes on March 1st.

Disaster Victims' Representatives Petition for Relief: After the eastern Xiaoshan sandy land was hit by the snow disaster, thousands of sand residents were displaced and in a dire situation. Moreover, the river flooded, and tens of thousands of acres of mature sandy land were submerged. The disaster victims have no way to make a living. Representatives have been sent to the province and county to petition, requesting that officials be sent to inspect the situation and provide relief.

Jade Mountain 83

The bandit communists of Jade Mountain were repelled by the training corps. After the communist bandits under Fang Zhimin and Shao Shiping were defeated in their lairs by the main forces, they took advantage of the situation to flee to Jade Mountain, first capturing Lingjiangpu, then Fangtou, endangering the county seat. Repeated requests for assistance were made, but due to the suddenness of the event, the provincial government had no troops to dispatch, so a special telegram was sent to Tang, the brigade commander stationed in Hekou, and Zhao, the regimental commander stationed in Shangrao, to devise a way to provide assistance. Regimental Commander Zhao, feeling that Raozhou was close to the bandit area and he could not divide his forces, personally led two companies to Yuzhen for support. At noon on the eighth, Zhou Jianping, the false army commander of the Red Army's Tenth Army, and Tu Zhennong, the false political commissar, led three regiments of infantry, one battalion each of machine guns, and teams of peasant Red Guards, women's Red Guards, and children's Red Guards, with over ten thousand bandits, to besiege Jade Mountain. Regimental Commander Zhao directed his troops to fight fiercely, holding out for five hours. Ultimately, outnumbered, they broke through the encirclement, sustaining minor injuries, and braved the rainy night to rush to Shangrao to gather his troops. He ordered Zhao, the regimental adjutant, to divide into two routes to encircle and suppress Jade Mountain, fighting fiercely all day, killing and wounding over a thousand communist bandits, and also killing the false regimental commander Mo Rongzheng and the false chief of staff Li Kedi. The bandit forces, unable to withstand the pressure, retreated in defeat towards the old base. The casualties of Regimental Commander Zhao's officers and soldiers were less than one hundred.

Shaoxing 84

The Banking Industry Decides to Reopen in Three Stages. After the Shaoxing banking industry ceased operations on a large scale, the industry association has now decided, according to regulations, to first reopen on March 1st, then again on the 6th, and continuously from the 11th. The draft industry regulations have also been carefully reviewed and finalized, and a general meeting will be convened on the 28th to jointly revise them. It has also been decided that interest arrears among colleagues should be increased by at least five percent, and that the exchange rate for Hangzhou remittances and silver dollars should be increased by at least five li, one li for copper coins, and two coins for copper rounds.

Pinghu 85

One Local Bandit Executed. The 10th Company of the Provincial Security Team stationed in Yaqian Town, Eastern Pinghu, captured a bandit named Jin Yousheng on the 25th in Sanyou River, three li west of Yaqian. When the troops went to capture him, the bandit resisted with gunfire, but was ultimately arrested. The bandit Jin confessed to robbery and kidnapping, details unknown. He was executed by firing squad in the eastern open area as a warning to the public.

Educational News

Important News

Ministry of Education Orders Notice of Relief Measures for Students in Unregistered Private Schools 86

The Ministry of Education has stipulated provisional measures for students admitted to unregistered private schools in various universities for the 1930 academic year. In addition to notifying public universities, colleges, and private vocational schools, instructions have also been issued to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, stating that public and registered private vocational schools and higher institutions should not, starting from the 1930 academic year, admit students promoted from unregistered private senior high schools or transfer students from unregistered private vocational schools and higher institutions. The Ministry has previously issued orders to comply with this. Recently, schools such as Shanghai Private Datong University have requested permission for provisional measures. Upon review of the original request, the reasons presented are not without merit. The following measures are now stipulated: (1) First-year students admitted to various vocational schools and higher institutions in the 1930 academic year who graduated from unregistered private senior high schools will be temporarily allowed to attend classes as auditors. When the educational administrative organs of various provinces and cities hold pre-admission examinations for graduates of unregistered private senior high schools around July of this year, they will be allowed to take the examinations nearby. After passing the examinations, their admission qualifications will be retroactively verified. (2) Transfer students from unregistered private vocational schools and higher institutions admitted to various vocational schools and higher institutions in the 1930 academic year will be temporarily allowed to attend classes as auditors. The entrance examination papers of each student should be sent to the Ministry for review. If deemed qualified, their admission qualifications will be retroactively recognized. The above measures are limited to students already admitted by various schools in the 1930 academic year. In addition to separate orders, this order is hereby issued to the said department for notification and compliance.

Anhui Provincial Education Commissioner Cheng Tianfang Resigns for Health Reasons 87

Cheng Tianfang, the Education Commissioner of Anhui Province, has been in office for two years, actively managing education. The academic atmosphere in Anhui has undergone a significant change. He recently resigned and arrived in Shanghai. A reporter inquired about the reasons for his resignation. Cheng stated, "I have been suffering from insomnia for the past two months, so I intend to relinquish everything and go to Lushan for recuperation. There is no other reason." Although he received earnest requests from within the province and from Anhui natives in Beijing and Shanghai to stay, he has firmly decided to resign and will not return. The original resignation letter from Cheng to the Executive Yuan is recorded as follows:

"Regarding the request for resignation: I, Tianfang, have been serving in the Anhui provincial government, responsible for educational administration, for over two years. Recognizing my heavy responsibilities and limited abilities, I have long considered retirement. Recently, my old insomnia has recurred. For two or three nights a week, I cannot sleep, and the next morning I experience dizziness and mental confusion, causing great suffering. Doctors advise that I am overthinking and need a long period of recuperation to restore my health. Therefore, my desire to leave is even stronger. If I continue to delay, it will be detrimental to both public and private interests. If illness prevents me from fulfilling my duties, it will affect the education of the entire province, for which I could not face the nation or Your Excellency. I believe Your Excellency originally entrusted me with the responsibility of rectifying the academic atmosphere. Over the past two years, I have devoted all my efforts to this, working day and night without relaxation. Although I have not achieved great success, the current situation is different from when I first arrived in Anhui. Students in various schools are now aware of their mistakes and are making learning their priority. The actions of occupying flags, distributing leaflets, assaulting teachers, and attacking government offices have ceased. Anhui is not a wealthy province, but over the past two years, provincial education funding has increased by nearly 600,000 yuan, and local education funding has increased by over 700,000 yuan annually. As a result, the number of schools and students has significantly expanded. These two achievements alone are enough to absolve me of blame. As for future efforts to improve student levels, enrich school content, and promote universal compulsory education and mass education, active measures are needed that require educational experts, which I, Tianfang, am not capable of. I should step aside. For these reasons, I respectfully submit my resignation, hoping for your prompt approval, so that I may be relieved of my duties as soon as possible. I await your command with utmost urgency and respect. Respectfully submitted to Jiang, concurrently President of the Executive Yuan."

Local News

The Chinese Language and Writing Society to be Established Tomorrow 91

The Chinese Language and Writing Society (Chinese Linguistic Association) was initiated by Chinese and foreign individuals in this city. Key figures include Professor Lin Heming of National Jinan University, Chief Engineer Chartley of the Huangpu Bureau, President Bu Jifang and Vice President Shen Siliang of St. John's University, Secretary Mak Zelin of the British and Foreign Bible Society, and Guoyu Luomazi (Gwoyeu Romatzyh) expert Li Yueh-wei. The purpose of the society is to study various issues related to Chinese language and writing, with special emphasis on the following tasks: (1) Researching the Guoyu Luomazi promulgated by the National Government. (2) Promoting the widespread use of the Romanization of Shanghai, Ningbo, Taizhou, Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xinghua, Xiamen, Shantou, Guangzhou, Hakka, and other dialects for phonetic notation and for popularizing mass education. (3) Promoting the widespread use of Zhuyin Fuhao (Bopomofo). (4) Promoting a perfect national phonetic shorthand system. (5) Studying Chinese minority scripts. (6) Studying various other problems related to Chinese language and writing. The society places particular emphasis on Guoyu Luomazi and phonetic scripts (or Zhuyin Fuhao). The society was initiated on December 21st of last year and has been in preparation for over two months. The inaugural meeting will be held at 1:00 PM on Sunday, March 1st, on the second floor of No. 23 Yuanmingyuan Road (near Sichuan Road). Chinese and foreign speakers will be invited to give speeches, and a photograph will be taken at 2:00 PM to commemorate the occasion. The society has purchased over ten types of Romanized books of various Chinese dialects, which are available in the library on the first floor of No. 23 Yuanmingyuan Road for reference by members and people from all walks of life. Those wishing to join the society are requested to attend on time.

Nanyang Middle School Invites Chu Minyi to Lecture 93

Nanyang Middle School has organized a lecture series for this semester. The first lecture will be given by Chu Minyi on the topic of "The Responsibilities of Middle School Students in the Period of Political Tutelage." The meeting will be held at 3:45 PM on the first day of the month in the school's alumni hall. All students will attend. After a formal greeting, Gu Yinming will deliver a welcome address, followed by Mr. Chu's lecture. First, he explained the essence of the Three Principles of the People and political tutelage, so that students could understand the importance of studying party doctrine. He then addressed the points that middle school students should pay close attention to, stating that they must understand the world situation and recognize their own position. They should not only focus on acquiring knowledge but also cultivate the ability to put it into practice. He said that the students, during this period of political tutelage, should concentrate on their studies, so that when they enter society in the constitutional era, they will be able to contribute greatly to the country. Finally, Gu Yinming summarized the main points of the lecture and invited everyone to stand and express their gratitude before adjourning.

Philippine Football and Basketball Teams to Visit Japan 96

▲ Early May

(Tokyo Correspondence) The football and basketball teams of the Philippine Demas University are renowned throughout the Philippines. The school's football and basketball teams maintained the national championship last year. In recent years, Japanese football and basketball skills have also made considerable progress, so the school has long wanted to visit Japan for a test. The school's physical education coach, Mr. Villa, has now been sent to Japan to contact the Tokyo Christian YMCA. After consultation, it was decided that Mr. Villa will lead 30 football and basketball players to Japan for matches in early May this year. They will stay in Japan for about three weeks. The first week will be devoted to ample practice, the second week will be for matches in the Kanto area, and the third week will be for matches in the Kansai area. It is planned that the basketball team will play against six universities - Waseda, Keio, Meiji, Rikkyo, Teikyo, and Shodai - from May 15th to 20th, while the football team will play against Teikyo, Waseda, and Keio universities, as well as the all-Japan champions, on the 15th, 17th, 19th, and 20th. The matches in the Kansai area are scheduled from the 23rd to the 26th. The strength of the two teams is equal to that of Japan's top teams, and it is expected that this expedition to Japan will result in an even split of wins and losses.

The Veritable Proof of Gold as Dung: Tao Zaidong 101

My friend, the boxing master Qian Yantang, is skilled in poetry. This past spring, after a heavy snowfall, he climbed to a high vantage point and gazed upon the snowscape of the Huangpu River. He penned the line: "No wonder the golden tide surges upward, before my eyes is a silver sea and a silver river." When he recounted this to me, I praised his wit. This led to a discussion about the value of gold versus silver, and touched upon the ancient saying that gold is like dung. Mr. Qian mentioned that during the Boxer Rebellion in the Gengzi year of the late Qing dynasty, he sought refuge in Baiyang Village, Yizhou. The atmosphere there was simple and unsophisticated, practically a paradise. It was said that during the Ming Dynasty, loyalty to the nation was highly valued. When Li Chuang became emperor, and the Qing army entered the pass, with Shunzhi ascending the throne, the village remained utterly ignorant. The village performed theatrical plays as usual, only stopping when the official proclamations arrived. For over two hundred years, until the Gengzi year of the Qing dynasty, the village remained as secluded as ever. At that time, a Prince Mou Bela also came to this village to avoid disaster. One day, his wife brought out a gold ingot and ordered the eunuch to exchange it with the villagers for tens of thousands of copper coins for daily use. The ingot weighed slightly over one tael. After inquiring throughout the village, no one was willing to exchange it. The eunuch was greatly astonished and repeatedly lamented the "great change in the hearts of the people of Cuiping Mountain" before leaving. At that time, several manure collectors were seen carrying their baskets, slowly approaching. There was a rural market nearby, the simplest form of exchange.

At the market, peasant households negotiated prices with manure collectors, each obtaining a certain number of thousands of coins for their baskets of fertilizer. They used the money to buy wine and meat. Mr. Qian personally witnessed this scene. He then reflected that the world is nothing more than a matter of "need". If there is a need, then dung is like gold. If there is no need, then gold is like dung. How can the current "golden tide" be an exception to the rule of need?

The Image Seized by Skilled Hands: Qing Zhuo 102

My neighbor is a family named Xu, whose residence is called Huaizu Hall. To the west of their dwelling, the master of the house is named Xiaoxia. His family fortune has declined, and his descendants are dwindling. However, in their room, they still have a sculpted image of the master, as perfect as new, as if one were conversing with him in person.

The Remodeling Doctor: ·Shadow·Fool 103

I recall one or two years ago, this newspaper published a daily, lengthy comic strip. In the beginning, there was a character called the Remodeling Doctor, a humorous figure that brought peals of laughter. Surprisingly, in America today, there actually exists a Remodeling Doctor. According to news from New York, at the Biology Research Institute of Cold Spring Harbor, Long Island, a group of biologists, all holding doctoral degrees, are engaged in research to remodel the human race. They hope that in the future, humanity will be more intelligent and physically stronger than it is today, and that lifespan will also be longer. Furthermore, this method has been proven through various experiments and is nearing the point of realization. When these doctors remodel humanity in the future, they will truly be worthy of the title "Remodeling Doctor."

The image is less than a foot tall, but it sits upright in proper attire, its whiskers and eyebrows lifelike, and one can almost hear it cough. Truly, only a divine hand could create such a wonderful creation, displaying the marvels of craftsmanship.

At the time this image was created, there was also Ge Shuliu of Nanli, whose image is still kept in a shrine. They open a room to change his clothes regularly, imagining his voice, laughter, and appearance, which leads to feelings of melancholy. Therefore, his image still exists today, even after more than thirty years, without the slightest bit of wear or damage. While it may be attributed to the embodiment of his spirit, it is also the ultimate expression of art.

I heard that the person who created these two images came from Wumen. He was heavily addicted to opium and slept soundly every day, not waking up until late at night. Therefore, his artistic endeavors were only carried out late at night in the quiet hours, accompanied by the flickering light of the opium lamp. It so happened that both the Xu and Ge families shared the same addiction, which made them even more congenial. Few others knew about this. Therefore, even today, no one knows the artist's name. I have repeatedly inquired among the elders, but no one can name him. It is truly regrettable that such a person's name has been lost.

However, it is said that when creating the images, he used a type of extremely pliable clay. He would sit opposite the person and, after gazing for a long time, his hands would begin to knead under the table while chatting and laughing normally, without revealing what he was creating. Initially, he would not show it to anyone. This went on for more than ten days before the image was completed. Those who saw it were greatly amazed, some suspecting that he possessed some secret knowledge. When I was young, I heard from my neighbor, Mr. Xu, that this person was fond of literature, especially skilled in calligraphy, adept at painting, and occasionally entertained himself with the qin. He was a nobleman's son. I wonder if anyone in Wuzhong can recognize him today. Someone with such accomplishments must have left his mark in more than just our county.

Mourning Dreams and Entrusting Sadness in Songnan: Zizai 104

"Feeling the past, I am now a person who mourns dreams. Do not let fleeting events be like the dust of the past. The heavenly realm of Tushita and the land of immortals, I fear Shuangcheng will be reborn as someone else." These are the verses inscribed by Zhuzhen Zhuang on the "Mourning Dreams in Songnan" painting. The "Mourning Dreams in Songnan" scroll was created by Zheng Wuchang after Wei Yibing passed away in Singapore, re-creating the nostalgic feelings of Hong Shusheng towards Qing Hu. The vastness of the sea and sky is exceptionally desolate and cold. Jin Xihou (Liang) wrote the title, and Yao Mangfu, Liu Yazi, Pan Lanshi, Zhang Daqian, Xie Yucen, and others wrote inscriptions. Mangfu used the "Narcissus" melody with the "Breaking Cassia Branch" Yuer music to write, "The spiritual rhinoceros always relies on the spring cuckoo. Butterflies gone, flowers fly, another year. Search everywhere in the painting. Facing the cold Song, count the fallen joys. The ripples are still rippling slowly. The alliance is empty. People are worthy of love. The soul is not far away. The wind is rotating. Vaguely under the moon, before the stars. Vaguely under the moon, before the stars. No more than the ethereal landscape painting of Yingqiu. Even if you understand the Zen of love, you still have not finished the mortal affairs. The depth of sorrow measured by the river and the sea. The river is like life before. The sea is separated from the sky. Sorrow gathers at the tip of the pen. How can it be like the river that can be overturned? The sea can also be filled." When the woman died in the southern border, Shi was in Hanyang doing politics. After hearing the news, she was dazed. She personally inscribed the stele and sent it to be planted on the grave. She also collected six chapters of Ding'an's poems to express her grief and hatred.

The poem says: "A short farewell to the lake and mountains outside the catastrophe. How many years will the seven stars repay me? Will the nine springs accept the praise of a madman? Daoyun's debating skills do not fall short of Quanquan. Slightly like riding a luan bird, drifting away. It is difficult to measure celestial beings with the naked eye. A hundred generations of ordinary people criticize me. Art is like a needle to the spirit, a face like Luoshen. Suddenly, I feel the years in the eastern mountains. I sealed my red tears and asked to return the car. Why use the heavenly flowers to protect the bell? It turns into spring mud to protect the flowers even more. I have failed both the flute and the sword. The wind, the luan, the crane, the mandarin ducks, three lifetimes. Only the Buddha understands the hard work. May the hatred of the sea be flattened one day. The fate of words is as deep as flesh and blood. The small screen, the red candle, talks about Dongxin. Writing books is not for cinnabar and lead. I have troubled you thousands of times to sing about Shanghai. The melody is touching and touching the spirits. After experiencing the catastrophe, the elixir is not completed. Gazing from afar, the night in the Central Plains. What other way to send this life." The mournful and bitter tune, as if hearing her voice.

The year before last, Shi was thirty years old. The woman sent a seven-character ancient poem, filled with blood and tears, which she could not bear to finish reading. However, the sincerity and inspiration of the two people are fully revealed in the words. The poem says: "Every year today is your birthday. I hate that I have no chance to sing the Nine Songs. What will I say when life reaches this point? After nine deaths, there is much regret. Counting the years, three years have become strangers. The southwest is blocked, how painful. Thinking of you a hundred times a day, my body is like a moth flying to the lamp. Sighing that fate is as thin as autumn leaves, lamenting the decline of the times, what can I change. From now on, I will understand the reason for karma. I will learn the ways of the monk from the plum blossoms on Mount Hua." It is heard that the woman left behind two volumes each of "Dream Non-Collection" poems and lyrics. Shi will collect and carve them, and distribute them to friends, hoping to repay the deceased in some small way.

The Ancient Books and Fengmu of China That I Have Seen 105

I recently read in "Free Talk" that the Yang family of Liaocheng, who owned the Haiyuan Pavilion collection, are unable to preserve it, and some of it has already flowed overseas. I secretly lament the daily demise of ancient books in our country. I also saw that someone was trying to sell a copy of the Song Dynasty edition of Han Changli's collection for 100,000 yuan. The price can be said to be enormous. The books that I have seen, while not as expensive as this, are still considerable in number. We poor scholars are already speechless upon hearing of them.

Years ago, I accepted an invitation from Mr. Wu of the same town to teach his children in Beiping. Mr. Wu's name was Jingci, styled Hengsun. His father was the manager of the Beiping HSBC Bank, so he had lived there for a long time. Mr. Wu had studied engineering in England. After returning to China, he served as an engineer on the Jingfeng Railway. Later, he returned home due to his father's death. Because his father had already accumulated wealth, he did not go out again. He was extremely fond of antiquity. He collected many antiques, calligraphy, and paintings, and ancient books were also one of them. When he bought ancient books, he had experts such as Li Mutang to appraise them, so he was never deceived. When I was in Beiping, someone wanted to sell a Song Dynasty edition of "Tang Wencui" and a Ming Dynasty edition of "Lou Gongkui's Collection" for 10,000 yuan. After Li appraised it, he paid the full amount. Mr. Wu showed me the two books. I saw that the paper of "Wencui" was very dark, and the margins at the top, bottom, and sides were not very wide. The last few volumes of the "Lou Collection" were incomplete and were supplemented with manuscript copies. I secretly wondered if the price was too high. However, according to Li, this 10,000 yuan was only enough to pay for the "Wencui" alone. The "Lou Collection" could only be considered a gift. Later, someone wanted to sell a Song Dynasty edition of "Li Shan's Commentary on the Selections of Refined Literature" for 6,000 yuan. I saw that the paper was as white as new, and the printing was also excellent. I thought that the paper and printing of "Wencui" were not as good as this, yet it was worth 10,000 gold. Therefore, this one asking for 6,000 yuan should not be considered expensive. After Li's appraisal, he said that although this book was good, there were many copies of it in China. As for the "Tang Wencui" that was purchased earlier, as far as he knew, only this one copy remained in the country. Even the Haiyuan Pavilion collection, which was known for its vastness, did not have this book. I then sighed that appraising ancient books was not easy. If it is not a book that currently exists in the country, and the actual number is known for sure, then its value cannot be determined. This further shows how precious this "Wencui" book is. Because I am concerned about the Yang family's situation, I have written this article. I hope that Mr. Wu and his descendants will protect it well and preserve one of the quintessence of our country.

Warmth in the Heart (376): Bao Tianxiao 106

Chapter Seventeen: The Art of Maintaining Youth: Emerald Blackened Eyebrows; The Desperate Search for Longevity: Golden Market for Horse Bones

Ye Tonghou pulled Hua Yuanchun to a pavilion in the back. He said, "Old Six, I just heard you say that you need to find a way to get money for travel expenses. Is the money you have enough for this trip?" Old Six said, "I'm trying to find a way. I think I can get some money from the little sisters." Ye Tonghou said, "How much do you need?" Old Six said, "Once I get to Beijing, I can get money from the big belly, Ah Jin. It's just the travel expenses on the way. Two or three hundred yuan should be enough." Ye Tonghou said, "Then I'll give it to you. Or, you can bring some food from the South as gifts for people. Take a hundred yuan first. I'll bring the other two hundred yuan tomorrow night." Old Six said, "No, Third Master, how can I take your money for no reason? Just take care of me a little when you get to Beijing. I've already talked to the new sister-in-law and asked her to borrow three hundred yuan. The interest is only four cents. Fortunately, once I get to Beijing, I can find a way to send it back." Ye Tonghou said, "Why bother? I'll be coming to Beijing soon. Can't you pay me back in Beijing? Or, you just don't want to use my money. You have to know that I don't have any other intentions." Hua Lao Liu said, "Third Master, you're so good to me, how can I not be grateful to you? Since that's the case, it saves me the trouble of finding a way elsewhere. It's all my fault for being so unclear-headed and so whimsical. If I don't do well in Beijing this time, I'll die in Beijing and never come back to the South." Ye Tonghou said, "Old Six, why do you have to say such final words? Sooner or later, everyone will die. Death is a road that everyone must go through. What's the difference between dying in Beijing and dying in Shanghai? A person is like a bird, flying to where it nests. When the sudden death comes, you just have to follow him. You say you'll die in Beijing, but who knows if I, Ye San, won't die in Beijing? We revolutionaries see death as insignificant. People who live long are just like living in a hotel, staying a few more days. There are also those mediocre people who seem to have come to the world for nothing, just for fun." Hua Yuanchun said, "We women should die even earlier. I think being an old woman is very boring." This made Ye Tonghou laugh. The next night, Ye Tonghou brought another two hundred yuan. This was an act of kindness in a time of need. Hua Yuanchun was naturally very grateful to Ye San, which saved him from having to find a way elsewhere. In fact, what Lao Liu had just said about entrusting the new sister-in-law was just a thought in his own mind. Hua Lao Liu was a master of wild talk. People always had some doubts about lending him money, just like the warlords borrowing foreign debt. Even if they said it nicely, what kind of industrial debt, financial debt, as soon as the money was in hand, it was sent to who knows where. Therefore, it was necessary to have solid collateral. Hua Lao Liu's borrowing was the same as the warlords' borrowing, and he was not in Shanghai. The words of the new sister-in-law were a bit unreliable.

Review of This Month's Yarn Settlement 114

▲Settlement volume reached 13,250 bales

The February yarn settlement took place at the beginning of the month, coinciding with the end of the lunar year. All the trading houses had completely ceased spot purchases as they closed their books, so the market was expected to decline. Prices hovered around 57 taels. Later, due to soaring gold prices, fluctuating exchange rates, and a turnaround in the Indian political situation, Indian cotton prices rose, and raw cotton prices steadily increased. As a result, the yarn market, being closely related, rose as well. The market closed for six days for the Lunar New Year holiday at a price of 170 taels and 0.08 yuan. This spring, when the market reopened, prices jumped by over 5 taels due to rising foreign cotton prices. Yarn prices increased dramatically. Buyers and sellers were deadlocked, and buying interest was extremely strong. To avoid risks, the exchange increased the special cash deposit for each newly purchased lot by 50 taels. At the same time, the exchange bought several thousand bales of 10-count coarse yarn from various factories and sold them short in near and distant months, which slightly reduced the heat. The 20th day passed relatively calmly, with the market closing at 8:30 PM. Only one round of cotton yarn trading occurred, but the situation remained tight. Due to reports that the United States would support silver prices, the gold market eased slightly. In the afternoon, the market fell by 4-5 taels, but soon cotton prices rose again, and a certain industrialist showed great enthusiasm for higher prices, exclusively purchasing domestic yarn in the last few days in preparation for receiving the goods. Although sellers had sufficient supply for delivery, they could not reduce the buying pressure, demonstrating the strong attitude of buyers. The last day of the month was the 26th, with prices soaring by 6.6 taels. The highest price was 178.4 taels, and the lowest was 155 taels. The difference within this month was 23.4 taels, a significant fluctuation. Spot yarn sales in the market were quite sluggish, with no excitement from any of the trading houses, due to high prices and slow sales. However, as the season is still at its spring peak, there is still hope for future development. The settlement volume was very high, totaling 13,250 bales. Among these, 9,250 bales were transferred through self-settlement, and only 4,000 bales were actually delivered. These included 550 bales of 20-count Shepherd, 2,250 bales of Five Blessings, 50 bales of 16-count Globe, 200 bales of Red Dragon, 450 bales of 10-count Three Sheep, 200 bales of Double Sheep, and 300 bales of Globe. Summary of This Month's Cotton Settlement 115

▲Quantity: 21,500 Dan (1 Dan equals 100 catties)

▲Shaanxi "Fire Machine" cotton was the most prevalent grade

February's settlement opened at 37 taels. The market was closed for six days due to the Lunar New Year holiday. During this period, the political situation in India improved, Gandhi was released, and European commerce showed some recovery. Therefore, Indian cotton prices rose sharply, gold prices soared, and exchange rates declined. Consequently, the silver-based calculation of foreign cotton became remarkably expensive. Speculators generally anticipated that the domestic cotton supply would be insufficient and foreign cotton imports would be unfeasible, which would inevitably drive up market prices. At the same time, buyers flocked to the market, and Japanese merchants aggressively purchased cotton, creating an extremely tight situation. On the 20th, both buyers and sellers were deadlocked. Sellers began to exhibit signs of panic. Later, the exchange authorities intervened to maintain stability, and Japanese merchants sold large quantities, which stabilized the market. The exchange increased the special cash deposit for each newly purchased load by 20 taels to reduce trading and avoid risks. Towards the end of the month, the dramatic rise in gold prices and the strength of Indian cotton led to prices reaching as high as 46 taels. The highest price for February was 45 taels. Total deliveries amounted to 21,500 dan. Shaanxi Fire Machine cotton was the most common grade delivered. The average price difference over the three delivery days was 44.5 taels. ▲Zhabei: Yesterday, sources from more than twenty locations arrived at the river, and the inventory in the river accumulated due to sluggish sales for several days, making shopkeepers hesitant to purchase. Northern white rice shows a precipitous fall, and the price has dropped another 10 cents. The price of 13 yuan per bag of rice may be considered the ceiling of the market. The supply of rice has slightly decreased and the interest in small amounts of rice is decreasing but buyers are pessimistic, leading to a sluggish appearance. Prices are similarly soft to Doo Tip rice. Small sales are sluggish and few small quantity transactions are occurring. The fixed-price contracts are weakened and the spot market is weak, with the most special grade barely opening at 12.20 yuan.

▲South Shanghai: Yesterday, about twenty boats were seen coming downriver. This area's sales are sluggish. The fundamentals of the market can be considered to have reached the low level because there is little interest in buying. The top grade of first-harvest short-grain rice has slightly increased, but everything else has decreased by 15 cents. The trend of Yangdu Tip is unfavorable, and retail sales have fallen by about 10 cents. Fixed-price contracts have weakened and the market has been shaded by lack of supply. The opening price of the special grade has been fixed at 10.50 yuan.

Flour and Wheat Plunge in Unison 117

▲The Impact of Foreign Wheat… Selling Pressure Remains Fierce

▲Flour: Yesterday, the flour market plummeted in the morning and afternoon sessions. This was because the quoted price of foreign wheat fell sharply. At this point, the initial hopes of buyers vanished like smoke. The large factories continued their multiple sales, and the amateur investors, who initially thought that flour and wheat prices would rise because of tight foreign exchange, had a seemingly reasonable surface-level justification, but trading at the exchange has no fixed standard, and most trading relies purely on leverage. Now that the sellers are mainly factory owners, the power of outside forces is inevitably controlled. The market was exceptionally weak all day due to extensive short-selling by outsiders. As a result, this month's contracts fell 3.5 cents compared to the previous day, March contracts fell 2.75 cents, April-May contracts fell 2.25 cents, and June-July contracts fell 3 cents.

▲Wheat: Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning and afternoon, contracts for all months showed sharp declines. The quoted price of foreign wheat fell by a huge 50-70 cents, which greatly shocked people. Selling pressure was extremely strong for a while, and contracts for all months fell in unison again. The market's trend is that the sellers have foreign wheat prepared, and in fact they disregard whether prices rise or fall. Because when the delivery period arrives, inventory must be available, and one needs to buy in order to pass smoothly. This is the reality and cannot be ignored. If the price of foreign wheat continues to fall step by step, then future fluctuations may again see the low prices of the previous month. As to deferred contracts, the mood was very weak, and people's hearts were greatly softened. As a result, the March contract fell 5 cents from the previous day, the April contract fell 10 cents, the May contract fell 6 cents, the June contract fell 8 cents, and the July contract fell 6 cents.

Local News

Domestic Railways Affected by Rising Gold Prices 122

▲Financial Difficulties of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway

The domestic railways have been greatly affected by the sharp rise in gold prices, which has led to a sudden increase in the cost of materials and the amount of principal and interest on foreign debts. Last year, gold prices rose by only one-third compared to the previous year, and the financial situation of the railways was already difficult to sustain. Now that gold prices have suddenly more than doubled, the financial difficulties have reached their peak. The Beijing-Shanghai Railway is close to the capital, and the situation is more certain and well-informed. Therefore, the details of the railway's financial situation this year are listed to inform those who are concerned about domestic railway administration.

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway's operating conditions have always been stable. However, since last year, due to the sharp rise in gold prices, the operating income has been insufficient to offset the losses caused by gold prices, and the financial situation has deteriorated. In May of last year, the railway was due to repay 116,000 pounds of maturing foreign debt principal. Since it was impossible to pay, the Ministry of Railways had to find ways to raise funds to pay for the 69,000 pounds of interest due in the second half of the year. The difficulty of the situation can be imagined. This year, gold prices are even more expensive than last year, and overdue and maturing domestic and foreign debt principal and interest are again approaching. The financial situation is unsustainable. The estimated amount to be paid by the railway this year includes the following items: (1) Foreign debt principal of 116,000 pounds due in May 1930, equivalent to approximately 2,552,000 yuan; (2) Foreign debt principal of 116,000 pounds due in May 1931, equivalent to approximately 2,552,000 yuan; (3) Foreign debt interest of 69,774 pounds due in May 1931, equivalent to approximately 1,535,000 yuan; (4) Foreign debt interest of 69,774 pounds due in November 1931, equivalent to approximately 1,535,000 yuan; (5) Outstanding profit to the Sino-British Company of 398,839 silver yuan; (6) Silver yuan 1,200,000 for the Ministry of Railways to raise funds for the second half of 1930 foreign debt interest; (7) Outstanding payment for various materials, totaling 1,079,555 silver yuan; (8) Repayment of the price of newly purchased locomotives of 117,000 pounds, equivalent to approximately 2,574,000 yuan. The total payment for the above eight items is over 13 million yuan. In addition, operating expenses are approximately 800,000 yuan per month, totaling 10 million yuan for the whole year. Including the previous eight items, the total expenditure is no less than 23 million yuan. The railway's operating income is only 13 million yuan per year, with a shortfall of over 10 million yuan. If this 10 million yuan is only addressed by thriftiness and no other means are found to increase income, the railway's operation will inevitably face bankruptcy. It is also heard that the railway's recent deposits are very small, and daily expenses are often stretched thin. The above is the situation of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. Other railways are roughly the same. It is heard that the Ministry of Railways' Business Operations Conference will open soon. It is hoped that the conference will not neglect this major issue and will quickly develop appropriate methods to remedy the situation.

Important Talk by Zhang Qun 123

▲Wu Peifu Has No Recent Activities

▲Election Office Will Start Operations Immediately

Mayor Zhang returned to Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday. Yesterday, a reporter from this newspaper met with him at the Municipal Government and asked him about the inside story of the Sichuan situation and other questions. According to Zhang, the central government has finalized the measures for Sichuan and appointed the provincial government members, which has been reported in detail.

▲Troops Stationed in Southern Shaanxi: Liu Cunhou's and Tian Songyao's troops never left Sichuan. Tian only sent personnel to incorporate the remnants of Feng Jun's troops in Shaanxi. The defense of southern Shaanxi was extremely weak, but I met with Yang Hucheng's representatives in Beijing, who said that Yang had sent one division and two brigades to station in southern Shaanxi. Wu Peifu is under the protection of Liu Cunhou's forces, has no command ability, and has no activities. The previous rumors that he would be invited to Beijing were not true.

▲Gongfa Board of Directors: Regarding the Riyue Bank incident, Zhang said that the municipal government found it difficult to proceed because the opinions of the creditors were inconsistent. Finally, it was decided to entrust four lawyers to voluntarily participate in the litigation for the creditors to maintain their legal rights. Since then, the creditors have not had any contact with the municipal government. The reporter then asked about reports of Yu Qiaqing's remarks that the roster of directors and shareholders of Gongfa Company had been handed over to the municipal government for safekeeping. He replied, "I just returned to Shanghai from Beijing and have not contacted anything. But no matter what, the directors of Gongfa should bear unlimited liability."

▲Preparing for Elections: Zhang also said that the Shanghai Election Office for National Assembly Representatives has been established, and the General Affairs Section has already started working. All internal tasks will be started on March 2nd. Internally, it is divided into three sections: the director of the General Affairs Section is concurrently held by secretary Li Dachao, the director of the Review Section is Feng Liutang, and the director of the Registration Section is Chen Bai.

▲Rumors of Trip to Japan: Recently, the Japanese side has been spreading rumors that Zhang will be appointed as the ambassador to Japan. The reporter asked about this yesterday. Zhang said that this rumor has been circulating for a long time and is absolutely untrue. It is even more ridiculous that the former chief of public security, Yuan Liang, will go to Japan to take up a post. Yuan was sent to Japan by the municipal government to investigate police administration and has no other mission.

▲Long-Term Police Savings: When the former chief of public security, Yuan, was in office, he established the Long-Term Police Savings program, entrusted to Jincheng Bank for safekeeping. It has been in operation for a year, with a balance of tens of thousands of taels. Later, due to difficulties in managing it, the program was terminated after Yuan stepped down, but the funds have not yet been returned. Yesterday, Zhang said that the funds need to be settled by Jincheng Bank before they can be returned. Yuan repeatedly stated when handing over his duties that the funds can be returned recently.

Population Statistics for the Public Concession Last Year 126

▲ 113,920 People per Square Mile

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession recently released population density statistics for the Public Concession for the past year, showing 113,920 people per square mile. According to the Council's report, the current population of the Public Concession is approximately one million, and is expected to increase to 1.5 million in fifteen years. The statistical report stated that based on the area of the central and northern districts of the Public Concession, the population density is 325 and a half per acre, or 209,650 per square mile. This record exceeds the population density of the most populous district of London, England, namely, Bethnal Green. Among the various districts, the eastern district has the highest population density, with 1494 people per acre. According to the Council's report, the survey method used these statistics was using the location of 46 police stations within the Public Concession as the area for calculating population density, which is more precise than the previous method of using the larger four districts as the area for calculating population density. The following table shows population statistics for the central district of the Public Concession. A comparison of last year's statistics with those from five years ago shows little change, but the methods used in the past were not very accurate or reliable. Negotiations Between the China Telegraph Administration and the North-China Daily News 127

▲ Regarding the Transmission of Telegraphs on the Shanghai-Fuzhou-Xiamen Submarine Cable

On the 22nd and 24th of this month, the North-China Daily News published two news reports regarding the Fuzhou and Xiamen telegrams, which were transmitted via land lines. The language was lengthy and the tone was biased, stating that business circles in Fuzhou and Xiamen felt extremely inconvenienced after the Ministry of Communications stopped the Great Northern and Great Eastern Telegraph Companies' rights to send and receive telegrams. The China Telegraph Administration's land lines are dilapidated, the transmission speed of the telegraph stations is slow, and there is no certainty. The telegram service is delayed and unable to handle the transshipment of submarine cable telegrams, and so on. The China Telegraph Administration believed that it fabricated facts, sensationalized the news, was unlike ordinary news reports, and seemed to incite public sentiment. It was suspected of falsely exaggerating the company's power and interfering with the government's administrative powers for the sake of the company. It sent a letter to the newspaper office for correction. However, the newspaper office replied that it only agreed to publish a brief summary. The director did not agree with this and argued reasonably, but the newspaper office ignored him. It is now reported that the director will report this matter to the Ministry of Communications for investigation.

Zhu Qinglan Arrived in Shanghai from the South 129

▲ To Report on the Disaster Situation in Shaanxi That He Witnessed

The disaster in Shaanxi is severe and rare in modern times. Zhu Qinglan, a compassionate savior, entered Shaanxi three times within the past year, braving hardships and personally going to the disaster areas and bandit-infested areas to investigate the disaster and provide relief for several months. He united with various charitable organizations and worked together to carry out various disaster relief efforts, focusing on both the symptoms and the root causes, and providing both physical and mental relief. Disaster-stricken areas such as Fufeng, Wugong, Xingping, Xianyang, Liquan, Qianxian, Qishan, and Sanyuan have benefited immensely. Last month, he returned from eastern Shaanxi to Tianjin to negotiate the transportation of materials for the drought relief Jinghui Canal project. Without rest, he went to western Liaoning to inspect the flood situation and guide winter relief efforts. On the 22nd of this month, he came south from Ping to Haizhou to participate in the groundbreaking ceremony for the Jiangbei labor relief Qiangshu River project. He will arrive in Shanghai within a day or two, with the aim of reporting the disaster situation in Shaanxi to people from all walks of life, and hoping to inspire everyone to make great efforts to complete the relief work in Shaanxi.

▲ Establishment of the North China Charity Federation Last spring, Zhu Qinglan, together with colleagues from various domestic charities in the north and south, escorted more than 4,000 tons of relief grain into Shaanxi to be distributed in the disaster area. Later, seeing the vastness of the disaster, he united various charity groups to establish the North China Charity Federation to work together and returned to Pingjin and Liaodong to raise urgent relief funds. People from all walks of life who personally heard Zhu's report from the disaster area enthusiastically provided assistance. During this period, more than 660,000 yuan was raised and brought to the disaster area to carry out relief efforts.

▲ Various Disaster Relief Efforts (1) Emergency Relief Distribution: In conjunction with the Shanghai Jisheng Association, Wutaishan Puji Buddhist Association, Xiaohui Study Society, Passionate Fengjihei Four Provinces Charity Association, and other charitable organizations, emergency relief was distributed in Xingping, Wugong, Fufeng, Qishan, Qianxian, Liquan, Hancheng, Sanyuan, Pucheng, Hanzhong, and other places. (2) Seed Distribution: Corn seeds were distributed in a total of 15 counties, and wheat seeds were distributed in a total of 7 counties. (3) Relief for Women, Children, and the Elderly: Temporary shelters were set up in the disaster areas. (4) Labor Relief: Disaster victims were employed to build roads and repair bridges. (5) Preservation of Farm Tools: Loans were provided to farmers in the disaster areas to prevent farm tools from being sold as fuel. (6) Promotion of Water Conservancy: The Jinghui Canal Water Conservancy Project was jointly organized with the China Foreign Famine Relief Association. (7) Education and Support: Disaster Children's Training Institutes, Women's Weaving and Dyeing Factories, and Textile Loan Offices were established. (8) Medicine and Clothing Distribution: Epidemic prevention and cold protection. (9) Burial of Starved Corpses: More than 6,000 starved corpses in the disaster area were buried in Mei County, and more than 3,000 in Qian County. (10) Winter Relief Soup Kitchens: The North China Charity Federation has established more than a dozen soup kitchens in the disaster areas of Xingping, Wugong, Fufeng, and Mei County, where approximately 40,000 people are currently receiving food every day.

The disaster situation in Shaanxi is severe, and universal relief is not easy. If charitable people from all over can provide more assistance, the suffering of the refugees in the disaster area will be reduced by one point. The severe winter has passed, and it is reported that wheat seedlings are growing in the fields in the disaster area, and there is hope for the future. However, at this time of year when the old harvest is exhausted and the new harvest has not yet come in, the suffering is greatest. The people of Shanghai have Zhu coming from thousands of miles away to personally describe the disaster situation in the disaster area, and after hearing it, they will surely have a way to comfort their compatriots in the disaster area of Shaanxi who are crying for food.

The six companies have planned to agree on and announce it before March 5, roughly according to the original amount of at least three-tenths of the increase.

Gonghe Wheel Dispute Heard Yesterday 133

▲ Tendency to Expand

The dispute between the old and new stewards on the Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Gonghe Wheel has been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now the situation is gradually expanding. The reporter went to various parties yesterday and recorded the following continued news.

▲ Jardine Takes on Mediation Jardine Matheson & Co. sent a letter to the Seamen's General Union yesterday morning, requesting that representatives be sent to the company to discuss a solution to the matter. The General Union immediately sent Chinese and English secretaries Liu Yuzhou and Li Zuyao, and worker representative Zhou Xiaoting, etc., to the company at 4 pm to negotiate with Jardine's shipping department head Ark and chief inspector Mading, etc. Jardine only agreed to reorganize the steward section of the Gonghe Wheel, but there was no result regarding the issue of removing Shen after two hours. Before the representatives went to Jardine, they first determined four requirements at the meeting: (1) Remove the compradore Shen Huating. (2) The company is responsible for resolving non-seamen. (3) The company should be responsible for compensating the losses of this dispute (ie, medical expenses, etc.). (4) In the future, the shipowner must be responsible for protecting all seamen on the ship. Seeing that Jardine had no intention of removing Shen, it was temporarily not proposed, so it broke up without results.

▲ Arrested Stewards Return to Shanghai A total of 24 old stewards on the ship were dragged ashore by the new steward side when they were beaten in Wuhu. Yesterday, Yang A'er, You Zhen'gui, Zhu Jinsheng, Bao Falin, Mo A'gui, Chen A'san, Zhong Jia Zhao, Chen Shunfu, Xu Delong, Xu Rongsheng, Chen Wu, Song Dingyuan, Wang Si, Wang A'sheng, Lu Lianjin, Sun A'sheng, Xu Jinshan, Song Dingxun, Jiang Aliang, Yu Wenhai, Ni Jinan, etc. returned to Shanghai on the Huangpu Baohuo two wheels. After arriving, they went to the union to report. There are still two people who have not returned to Shanghai, and the injured Yang Guisheng, Lin Shouzhi, and Wu Zeli have been sent to Tongren Hospital. It is reported that the injuries are quite serious.

▲ The Workers' Committee Goes to Wuhu to Thoroughly Investigate The nine new stewards, etc., who committed the crime in Wuhu have been transferred to the Wuhu Court and detained for interrogation because the police chief searched out the weapons at the scene. The Shanghai branch of the Seamen's Union, in order to understand the truth of this case, specially sent committee members Cheng Yaxin, Wang Shenxiu, Ren Shaoqing, etc. to Wuhu to conduct an on-site investigation, so as to verify the matter. Committee member Cheng, etc., left Shanghai for Wuhu last night.

▲ Passengers Come to Shanghai to Testify Shen Huating, compradore of Gonghe, etc., were escorted to the local court at 3 pm the day before yesterday. Yesterday, after a preliminary trial by Prosecutor Wu, he ordered Shen Huating, Wang Jinquan, and Yu Dequan to be released on bail first, and Ge Baoshu was detained. In the afternoon, the water patrol room transferred the two steward leaders, Ding Yongchang and Hu Hanzhang, to the court, and Prosecutor Wu still ordered them to be detained for interrogation. Regarding this case, the passengers on the same ship all witnessed what happened. At the moment, the eldest son of Chairman Lu of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, and Chen Liquan, former member of the Jiangxi Provincial Government, etc., are all willing to come forward to testify. Both of them landed in Nanjing, saying that they can be responsible for reporting to the Central Government. Passenger Lan Junheng, especially for this case, is willing to be a notary public. After coming to Shanghai, he lived in Dayun Inn at Sanyangjing Bridge, in preparation for testifying in court.

▲ The Union Reports to the Central Government The Seamen's General Union has reported the course of this case to the Central Government to ask for instructions. Once the reply arrives, negotiations will be made with Jardine, etc. The Shanghai Seamen's Branch also sent a fast mail telegram yesterday, announcing the ins and outs of the case to all public organizations in the country, requesting unanimous assistance and upholding justice.

▲ Gonghe Has Already Sailed Yesterday The Gonghe Wheel loaded cargo and passengers yesterday and sailed to Hankou. All the old stewards are still serving on the ship.

Records of the General Meeting of Various Trade Guilds in the Customs Brokerage Industry 136

▲ Customs Clearance for Cotton Yarn and Cloth Factories Requires Permits

▲ Recommend Shi Zhikun and Others to Study Business Tax

The Shanghai Municipal Transshipment Customs Brokerage Industry Association convened a meeting of various trade guilds yesterday to discuss the impact of the collection of unified taxes on cotton yarn and cotton cloth on the industry, as well as the business tax issue, etc. More than 100 representatives from more than 100 companies attended. Chairman Shi Zhikun delivered the opening speech, stating that since the Ministry of Finance started collecting unified taxes on the first day of this month, various cotton yarn and cloth factories, based on the unified tax rate regulations, no longer need to pay customs duties, so they no longer go to the customs to copy and pay for the black corner permits that they have been using. However, the customs believe that yarn merchants do not pay customs duties and do not copy permits, so they must reopen the boxes for customs inspection. Thus, the first inspection procedure at the unified tax office has already been done, and the customs want to inspect the goods again, which is extremely troublesome. In addition, the tax money filled in by the industry is huge and poses various risks. After discussion, it was agreed that this type of business is extremely dangerous, and if strict measures are not taken, the industry will suffer greatly. It was decided on the spot: (1) All goods from cotton yarn and cloth factories without permits will not be cleared on their behalf. (2) Send the above-mentioned reasons and resolutions to the Yarn Factory Federation and the Cotton Cloth Association to inform the factories to quickly complete the permit procedures. (3) From March 1, if the factory does not copy the black corner permit, in order to avoid cumbersome procedures and risks, all customs clearance will be suspended on their behalf. (4) Those who violate the above-mentioned resolutions will be fined one tael of silver per package. (5) Recommend Shi Zhikun and You Senting to visit the tax commissioner together with representatives of the business guild to state the difficulties of inspecting goods without permits and whether the inspection can be exempted. (6) Request the Unified Tax Bureau to print the customs declaration forms according to the format in the bureau and not to allow the bureau to designate someone to sell them at a higher price, so that the industry suffers more losses. Next, the issue of business tax was discussed, and more than 30 people including Shi Zhikun were appointed as specialized committee members to conduct joint research and present the results of the research to the superiors for adoption. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Dockworkers Are Allowed to Be Exempt from Business Tax 137

▲ The Ministry of Finance Approves the Various Industries Tax Rules Conference

The Shanghai Municipal Various Industries Tax Rules Conference notified various trade guilds yesterday: "Dear Sirs, our association previously believed that dockworkers in various industries do not engage in buying and selling activities, and it seems appropriate to exempt them from business tax to avoid duplication. After we telegraphed to report the matter for verification and handling during the cold weather, we received a fast mail telegram from the Ministry of Finance of the National Government today, No. Bin 5754, which stated: 'The Various Industries Trade Guilds Tax Rules Research Committee of Shanghai City has been informed of the cold weather telegram. The Ministry is currently reviewing the draft business tax regulations for the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in detail. If there are any violations of the Ministry's established outline, they should be checked and corrected. As for dockworkers who only buy and do not sell, since they have no business income, they are not subject to collection, and the business tax regulations sent by the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang do not list this item. There is no need for disturbance. Based on the previous situation, in addition to ordering the Finance Departments of the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to be informed, we hereby inform you.' Due to the Ministry of Finance's seal, etc., we have sent a separate letter in addition to this notification, hoping that you will check it."

Pan Gongzhan Discusses the Prohibition of Stores Concurrently Operating Savings 138

▲ Please Return the Measures to Be Approved by the Bureau First

A reporter from the New Voice News visited Pan Gongzhan, the director of the Social Affairs Bureau, yesterday regarding the prohibition of ordinary stores concurrently operating savings. According to him, the bureau was ordered to prohibit such activity, so it is difficult to be lenient. After receiving the order, the relevant stores should stop collecting savings deposits immediately, but they should not stop paying out. As for the application for reimbursement measures, the relevant companies and stores should follow the instructions and report to the bureau within ten days of receiving the document. They can only proceed after the bureau approves the application. They are not allowed to stop paying out or reduce payments without authorization, causing depositors to suffer losses. The reporter then asked how to handle the fixed-term deposits that have not yet matured. It is said that this can be handled according to the usual practice of current deposits. The reporter then asked why the Social Affairs Bureau did not prohibit the reading savings of the World Bookstore, as rumored. It was answered that the reading savings of the World Bookstore was reported to have been stopped in June last year. As for the savings department of the bookstore, it is related to the savings of the employees and shareholders of the bookstore, and most of the reading savings depositors have also withdrawn their principal and interest. Those who are unwilling to withdraw will be transferred to the World Commercial Savings Bank for deposit. As for the World Commercial Savings Bank, which is run by the bookstore separately, it is heard that the Ministry of Finance sent personnel to investigate and has received a license. However, since it has not yet opened for business, it should not absorb savings deposits first. Moreover, the savings deposits of reading savings depositors who have not withdrawn their savings deposits should be returned uniformly according to the law. Savings can only be handled according to the law after the bank is officially opened. The same applies to other stores that concurrently operate savings. In short, whether a company or store has credit is one thing, and ordinary companies and stores cannot concurrently operate savings is another. We cannot recognize that it has credit and allow it to operate savings under this name. Even for banks, it is not the case that all can operate savings. To operate a savings bank, it must be registered as a bank, set aside capital separately, and formulate separate articles of association, stating that all directors and co-managers are fully and infinitely liable, and its investment methods and balance sheets of assets and liabilities should be reported to the government on a regular basis and disclosed to the public before it can be approved to operate savings. Otherwise, a bank that operates savings in the name of a registered limited liability company absorbs savings deposits, and if an accident occurs, it will only bear limited liability, and depositors will suffer too much loss. As for companies registered in foreign countries, as long as they set up shops in China, they should re-register as branches with the competent Chinese government authorities, otherwise they cannot be recognized as limited liability companies.

Shanghai County Local Pacification Meeting Resolutions 141

The Shanghai County Local Pacification Bureau convened a local pacification meeting the day before yesterday (a summary was reported yesterday). The complete resolutions of that day are now recorded below. The meeting began with a report from the chairman and bureau director, Yan Shenyu, who stated that the purpose of convening the meeting was to discuss the procedures for carrying out local pacification. He mentioned that some people believe that local pacification should be carried out in areas with banditry, which is a misconception. While local pacification should indeed be carried out in areas with banditry, with attention paid to suppression, attention should also be paid to prevention in areas without banditry. Therefore, the current effort is being carried out uniformly across all counties as decided by the provincial government. This county, having received the order to establish a Local Pacification Bureau within one week, has complied by establishing the bureau within the deadline and notifying all districts to establish sub-bureaus and commence operations. He then presented a summary of the planned outlines for local pacification procedures for detailed discussion and comments. The following resolutions were passed: (1) The bureau director proposed a plan for discussing the outlines of the local pacification procedures for each sub-bureau. The resolution was passed with modifications. (2) The bureau director submitted a proposal for discussion on propaganda plans for each sub-bureau and school. The resolution was passed with modifications. (3) Director Yao proposed that for the sake of lasting benefit from this local pacification effort, magnetic doorplates should be manufactured for discussion. The resolution was passed: (i) to manufacture magnetic doorplates; (ii) to implement this first in urban areas; (iii) for the county to determine the size and style of the doorplates, as well as the implementation timeline, and to inform each district to follow accordingly. (4) Director Yao raised the concern that due to the mobile nature of boats, it may be difficult to obtain guarantees for boat households during this effort. He proposed seeking guarantees from shops instead. The resolution was to submit this to the province for approval. (5) Director Fu proposed implementing mutual guarantee and joint liability, with each neighborhood unit consisting of five households. However, considering the existing neighborhood organization in each district, where some neighborhoods have more than seven households or fewer than five due to location, he asked how to remedy this. The resolution was to submit this to the province for instructions. (6) The first district head proposed that the water police should assist in the investigation of boats. The resolution was to send a letter to the water police district headquarters requesting assistance. (7) The county council deliberated on the matter of assistant staff for the Local Pacification Bureau, proposing that each district nominate candidates to the county for selection and appointment. The resolution was to have each district nominate one person by March 2nd for county review and appointment. (8) The fifth district head proposed that each district's security forces should earnestly cooperate in the local pacification effort and conduct patrols three times a month. The resolution was for the county to issue an order to all security corps to earnestly comply.
