The People's Livelihood Improvement Association's Fifth Meeting Yesterday 143

▲Resolution to request the government to effectively implement the Factory Law

The People's Livelihood Research and Improvement Association continued its fifth discussion meeting yesterday, with over forty representatives from various parties in attendance. The chairman was Zhong Keto. The morning session discussed the relationship between labor welfare and government labor policy, while the afternoon session discussed the relationship between labor welfare and the organization of labor movements. The details of each session are recorded below.

▲Morning Discussion A. Zhu Maocheng presented the content of the Factory Law and points to note: (1) Factory meetings are not intended for joint management by capital, but to resolve misunderstandings and disputes. (2) Reduce child labor and provide relief to unemployed adult workers. (3) Working hours should be based on the principle of eight hours. (4) Criticize the petition of the China Industrial Federation as non-compliant. (5) The Factory Law is the result of the efforts of all parties for labor over the past ten years, and efforts should continue in the future. B. Lin Donghai presented the key points for the implementation of labor laws in various countries: 1. Unified and stable government. 2. Social issues are compatible with economic conditions. 3. Both labor and management have knowledge. 4. Both labor and management have ethics. 5. There are effective inspection methods. He further pointed out the shortcomings of factories in China, due to the lack of definite standards for wages, working hours, bonuses, child labor, and pensions. C. Gu Bingyuan raised two difficulties in mediating labor-management disputes: 1. Factories run by foreign merchants are not subject to mediation. 2. There is no standard for wages. He also advocated for the recovery of concessions and the training of specialized inspection personnel after the implementation of the Factory Law. The main points of the discussion were: 1. Request the government to effectively implement the Factory Law and establish an agency to manage the Factory Law. 2. Request the government to train inspectors. 3. Request the government to recover concessions as soon as possible. 4. Request the Public Concession and the French Concession to cooperate with China in implementing the Factory Law.

▲Afternoon Discussion A. Dai Leren proposed discussions on: 1. Whether past labor movement organizations were due to workers lacking knowledge. 2. How those engaged in labor welfare work should guide workers in organizing trade unions. 3. What kind of organizations can assist the labor movement. B. Chen Qitian raised the question of why, in foreign factories, units are organized by factory or by region, while the Factory Law in China stipulates organization by district. C. Sun Miaoyun presented opinions on the current organization of trade unions. D. Deng Yuzhi proposed that the association should provide side-by-side assistance to the labor movement and include more materials on labor movements and organization in worker education programs. Finally, Chen Zongcheng proposed that the government's protection of workers should not only focus on factory workers and large industrialists, because in addition to factory workers and large industrialists, the lives of miners and rickshaw pullers are even more difficult, and the association should petition the government to provide legal protection for them. Regarding previous questions, four review committees were set up for review, including the first group for worker life and worker education, the second group for industrial issues and cooperative enterprises, the third group for the relationship between worker welfare and government labor policy, and the fourth group for Christianity and labor programs.

▲Today's Agenda Today's discussion topic is Christianity and people's livelihood issues, and the afternoon will be used to discuss and resolve the reports of each review committee.

Rice Industry Bushel Ticket Affixing Stamp 144

The Shanghai Bean and Rice Trade Association issued a notice yesterday to various bean and rice industry groups and trades, stating: "Regarding bushel tickets, delivery barcode slips, and other items that are not invoices, and should not be affixed with stamp tax, this association has previously sent a letter to the Jiangsu Shanghai Precious Stamp Tax Bureau, forwarding it to the Ministry of Finance for exemption. A reply has now been received stating that the three types of documents have been forwarded to higher authorities for review. Before a clear order is received, they will be temporarily exempted from inspection. As for formal bushel tickets, which contain the name of the goods, quantity, price, and amount of silver, it is undoubtedly necessary to affix stamps. However, if the stamp tax fee should be acknowledged by the seller, the responsibility for affixing stamps should still be borne by the buyer in their place, in order to assign responsibility. Regarding the procedures for both buyers and sellers, your association should notify the trades and rice merchants to follow these regulations." In accordance with this, the seventh executive committee of this association resolved that the responsibility for affixing stamps on formal bushel tickets should be borne by the buyer, but the stamp tax fee should be borne by the seller and deducted when settling accounts, starting from March 1st. It has been decided on file. In addition to sending notices to the rice industry associations to inform the merchants to comply, this notice is hereby issued to all our colleagues, hoping that all formal bushel tickets will be affixed with stamp tax, and the stamp tax fee will be deducted from the seller when settling accounts. This is specially notified.

Labor Dispute at China Metal Factory Resolved 145

▲Workers Resumed Work Yesterday

The labor dispute that occurred at the Japanese-owned China Metal Manufacturing Factory on Jixiang Road, Hongkou, in this city, has lasted for more than a month. The Social Affairs Bureau has repeatedly mediated, but without results. On the afternoon of the 26th, the bureau's fifth mediation committee held a mediation session for this case. After a long discussion, a signed agreement was reached. All workers held a general meeting yesterday morning, resolving to return to the factory and resume work, and petitioned the municipal government to order Tang Zhenchao and others to compensate the workers for their losses in this incident. The signed agreement is recorded below. The dispute between the parties concerned is a dispute over factory closure and changes in the work system. The committee convened a mediation session, and the parties agreed to sign an agreement, which is recorded as follows: (1) The factory shall comply with the bureau's order to reinstate worker Lin Enkang. Wages for the period of the work stoppage shall be paid from the date of the second order (January 21st). (2) Wages for all workers during the work stoppage shall be paid at half rate. In addition to their due wages, apprentices shall be given a food allowance of two yuan each by the factory. (3) The steel finishing and polishing departments shall be changed to a piecework system. The wages for each piece shall be increased by 30% in accordance with the regulations of the former Huachang Factory. (4) If the actual wages earned by workers calculated on a piecework basis are less than 85% of their current daily wages, the factory shall make up the difference. (5) Except for the departments mentioned in item 1, the wages of other departments such as printing, coppersmithing, making, carpentry, temporary workers, and female workers shall be paid in accordance with the original wages before being changed to a piecework system. (6) When there is no work for piecework, wages shall be paid as usual. Wages shall be paid at half rate for all holidays stipulated by the factory (two days per month). (7) If work is suspended for a full day due to the repair of machinery or the replacement of molds, wages shall be paid as usual. (8) The factory shall give all workers a bonus equal to one month's wages at the end of each year. However, for piecework workers, 85% of the current daily wage shall be given. Those who have worked for less than one year shall be paid on a pro rata basis. (9) Workers who do not take leave within one month shall be given one day of leave as usual, and wages shall be paid as usual. (10) In addition to the wages they are due, apprentices in the steel finishing and polishing departments shall be given a subsidy of one yuan per day by the factory. (11) Matters not expressly stipulated in this agreement shall be handled in accordance with the laws of the Republic of China. This agreement has been agreed upon and signed by the representatives of both parties and shall be regarded as a labor agreement between the parties in dispute.

Famous Actress Qin Xuefang Dies of Illness 147

▲Passed Away the Day Before Yesterday, Full Funeral Yesterday Afternoon

▲Elderly Mother and Younger Sister Grief-Stricken

Qin Xuefang, a famous female performer from Beijing and Tianjin who specialized in qingyi roles, was known as one of the "Four Diamond Generals" along with Zhang Eyun, Ma Yanmei, and Jin Shamei, forming a counterpart to the "Four Great Dan" Mei, Shang, Xun, and Cheng. Since marrying her husband several years ago, Qin has resided in Shanghai. Her presence has been absent from the stage for a long time. She recently contracted a lung disease and died the day before yesterday (the 26th) at 10:00 AM at her residence on Route Massenet. She was only 27 years old. It is truly lamentable that such a beautiful woman died so young. Her elderly mother and younger sister, who lived with her, were overcome with grief. Qin was a Muslim and her funeral was held yesterday at 12:00 PM according to Islamic rites. The coffin was temporarily placed in the Qingzhen Temple in Rihui Port. Qin's original name was Ma Jinfeng, and she was originally from Shandong. Her father was a former Qing dynasty scholar who was honest and did not engage in production. After his death, the family was impoverished, and the mother and daughter had no way to make a living, so they learned opera from a teacher. She performed at the Great World and Qiankun Theatre, in the same troupe as Wang Biyun and others. Later, she went to Beijing and studied under Wang Yaoqing. Not long after, she joined a troupe in Tianjin, where she was greatly appreciated by Li Huangpi, and her reputation rose. She was ranked as one of the Four Diamond Generals.

New Record for Extortion: Extortion of 100,000 Yuan 148

▲Chuan Zhihong Initially Ignored

▲Later Received a Phone Call Inviting Him to Negotiate

▲Detective and Informant Disguised as Waiters

▲Six Extortionists Arrested Together

Fu Zhihong, a native of Ningbo who is engaged in construction in Shanghai, residing at No. 1334, East West Waide Road, has received three threatening letters by mail from January 30th to February 7th, demanding 100,000 yuan. This huge amount has broken the new record of extortionists. The third letter included two bullets and contained strong language, stating that if he did not comply, his son would be killed. Chuan initially ignored them, but at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, he suddenly received a phone call instructing him to negotiate in Room 411 of the Shenzhou Hotel on Fuzhou Road. The room was marked with a Wu surname plate. Chuan reported this to the Huishan Police Station, which sent Detective Zhang Zhiqin and informant Xu Yongyuan, disguised as waiters, to the hotel to act as tea waiters. Fu then ordered Chen Huatang to go as scheduled. Upon entering the room, he was greeted by Ningbo natives Wu Abao and Zhang Yiming. After inquiring that Chen was Chuan's representative, Zhang first said, "Mr. Wu has not arrived yet, please sit down for a while." Wu then said, "Mr. Fu is too arrogant to delay until now without replying." At this time, Ningbo natives Wu Wanggen, Ge Yongchang, Zhang Agen, and Chai Xingfu entered the room one after another. Ge spoke first, saying, "We have already decided to reduce the amount to 50,000 yuan, and now it has been reduced to 20,000 yuan, which cannot be less." Chen then explained that Fu was not wealthy and could find a way to raise 1,000 yuan, but it was impossible to bear a huge amount. Ge continued, "We have already spent 1,000 yuan on this matter. Since you are here, we will give you face and ask Fu to pay 15,000 yuan to settle the matter." Chen said that he could not make a decision and would go back to discuss it. He got up and left the room, and the detectives disguised as tea waiters rushed in and arrested Wu and the other six people together. Yesterday, they were taken to the Special District Local Court. Judge Feng Shide interrogated them. Fu and Chen appeared in court and recounted what happened, presenting the letters and bullets as evidence. Questioned Wu confessed that this matter was done by Zhang Agen, Chai Xingfu, and a runaway "long-legged A-San." Zhang and Ge Yongchang both confessed that they were invited to the hotel by Wu Deming. Wu Wanggen confessed that he was invited by Wu Agen. Zhang Yiming confessed that he went with Wu, but they all denied knowing who wrote the threatening letters. The judge ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody for further interrogation.

Divorce Case Against the Wife of a Chef at the Da San Yuan Restaurant Dismissed 149

▲Plaintiff Admits to Adultery

▲Right to Divorce Belongs to Defendant

▲Did Not Want to Publicize Family Scandal

▲Tolerated Wife to Preserve Family Honor

Hu Guanfu, a chef at the Da San Yuan Restaurant, was sued for divorce by his wife, Hu Yang, in the Special District Local Court. She claimed that Hu had a hidden illness, making him incapable, and that he instigated his brother-in-law, Wang Xuetang, to commit adultery with her. Hu retained lawyer Hong Shihao to defend himself and offered to have a forensic doctor examine him. Judge Xu Wenrong ordered a forensic examination before making a decision, which was previously reported. During the continued interrogation, Judge Xu informed both parties that the Special Court did not have a forensic doctor of this kind at the moment and that the examination would be waived. According to the plaintiff, Hu Yang, her husband did have a hidden illness, and they only had intercourse for three days after the marriage, and she never took off her clothes. Moreover, the defendant's sister, Wang Hu, repeatedly encouraged her to sleep with her husband, Wang Xuetang, in order to continue the family line. The defendant's claim of a hidden illness was therefore well-founded. Therefore, she was unwilling to maintain the empty name of husband and wife and requested that the divorce be granted and that the dowry be returned. The defendant, Hu Guanfu, also continued to deny that he had a hidden illness, saying that he could be examined at any time. He had not heard of any ambiguity between the plaintiff and Wang Xuetang after she privately left home. The child she bore, whose seed it was, was even more difficult to determine. But he did not want a divorce and requested that they be ordered to live together. After the interrogation, the parties were instructed to begin their arguments. Lawyer Wang, representing the plaintiff, said that the plaintiff and the defendant had only lived together for three days and did not take off their clothes. Moreover, looking at the defendant's appearance, it was clear that he had a hidden illness. For three years, he not only failed to fulfill his duties as a husband but also encouraged adultery, instigating his brother-in-law to perform his husbandly duties. For such a nominal couple, the law, in order to protect women's rights, should grant a divorce. Defendant's lawyer Hong Shihao argued that the plaintiff's allegations were nothing short of a fantastic novel. They could be sensational if said in a tea shop, but they were too bizarre and unfounded when viewed with a legal eye in the dignified courtroom. The claim that she did not take off her clothes for three nights was entirely empty talk. Even if it could be proven, it could not be inferred that he had a hidden illness. It would be even more absurd to determine that he had a hidden illness based on his unattractive appearance. Since the plaintiff admitted to adultery with Wang Xuetang, the right to request a divorce naturally belonged to the defendant. Now, the defendant did not want to publicize the family scandal, and marriage was not easy, so he tolerated her to preserve family honor. How should the adulterous woman repent? She believed that since she had committed adultery, she could request a divorce from her husband, which was ridiculous. Therefore, he requested that the plaintiff's suit be dismissed and that she be ordered to live with the defendant. Xu Mu, the prosecutor, then came to court to state his opinion. Judge Xu opened the court yesterday and ruled to dismiss the plaintiff's suit. The plaintiff shall bear the costs of the litigation.

Unexplained Death of a Woman 150

▲Rumored to Have Died from Taking Medicine for Abortion

▲Truth Will Be Revealed After Examination This Morning

Yesterday morning, an unexplained death of a woman occurred at the home of Taoist Gao at No. 13, Ping An Lane, East End of Route Joffre, French Concession. At that time, there were rumors in the streets, and someone secretly reported to the police station. The police chief, upon hearing the news, immediately sent a detective to investigate and transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall morgue for examination. This reporter, upon hearing the news, rushed to investigate. The exterior of the lane was quite neat, but the interior was full of bungalows. Moreover, there was a tiger stove at the entrance of the lane, and the inside was extremely dirty. After several twists and turns, the reporter inquired and found No. 13. The house was a three-room, two-wing bungalow, completely old-fashioned. The courtyard was very wide. After entering the room, there were Taoist scriptures and Zhu boxes, and the furnishings filled the hall, indicating that it was the residence of a Taoist. Inside the reception room, there were three or five young men wearing gabardine coats, who were sitting around the table having dinner. When they saw the reporter, they looked at each other in surprise. When the reporter inquired, one of the young men showed an unhappy expression and answered evasively, saying that the house was No. 3, the dead woman's name was Chen, from Liuhe, 30 years old, and she had been a widow for a long time. Ten years ago, she became acquainted with Gao Yunshan, who lived there. Gao was a local, 28 years old. The house was Gao's ancestral property. Since becoming acquainted with Chen, they had raised two daughters and one son together. Gao himself used to work in a printing shop, but he has been unemployed for six or seven years. He has never been a Taoist. Later, because he had spare rooms, he rented them to Taoist Gao Hongshou, so it was mistakenly rumored that Gao was also a Taoist. As for the cause of Chen's death, it was because she gave birth to a daughter on the 9th of this month and then fell ill. She died of postpartum hemorrhage at 5:00 PM yesterday (the day before yesterday). This morning (yesterday morning), because of dealing with funeral affairs, there were many idlers standing at the entrance of the lane, who were spotted by patrolling police officers. Moreover, because a passerby falsely reported that she was murdered, the police station, for the sake of caution, transported the body to the morgue to be examined. After the examination, they allowed the body to be coffined. The reporter found his words extremely contradictory, and because it was a matter of human life, it could not be ignored. He returned to the morgue to inquire, but the information on the corpse form was completely inconsistent with what the young man said. The form stated that the plaintiff was Yuan Yunlin, the father of the deceased, and the defendant was Gao Lansheng. The witnesses were Yuan Changde and Gao Yuezhen. Yuan was the deceased's younger brother, and Yuezhen was the deceased's daughter. The deceased's name was Yuan Xiaoding, 36 years old. The cause of death was from taking medicine for an abortion. However, the deceased's face was purplish-blue, which resembled poisoning. What is the truth will be known after the examination today.

Conviction of Kidnapping Gang 152

▲Once Kidnapped Flour Merchant Ding Ziren

▲Committed 15 Cases in the French Concession

▲Cases in the Public Concession Not Included

Chen Shuxing, Zhang Wu (also known as Yang Wu), Chen Kaiqiang, and other members of a kidnapping gang, armed with weapons, kidnapped Ding Ziren, the manager of the Fuxin Flour Mill, at 10:30 AM on December 19th in the Public Concession on Moganshan Road. They hid him in Fengxian, Pudong. The authorities were informed and rescued the hostage. Chen and other bandits opened fire to resist arrest and fled to Shanghai, where they committed robberies in the French Concession. Detectives and inspectors Jin Jiulin and Li Yaolong, deputy detectives Qian Yumin and Jin Gen, Zhang Ziying, and police officers Zhou Buguang and Xu Guilin of the French Police Department detected and arrested Chen and the other three bandits, as well as suspects Xu Xiaohuaizi and Zhang Jinlin. Two Mauser pistols and one handgun were found on Chen and the other bandits, and they were taken to the police station. After interrogation, Chen and the other bandits confessed that in addition to the kidnapping of Ding Ziren, they had committed 15 robberies in the French Concession from May of last year to January of this year, including: Du Xingqiu's cigarette and paper shop at No. 28 Xinglong Street, Xujiahui Road; Jiang Rongfu's cigarette and paper shop at No. 471 Xujiahui Road; Sun Shaofang's cigarette and paper shop at No. 245 Xujiahui Road; Qingfeng Sauce Garden at No. 616 Xujiahui Road; Pan Caibao's dried goods store at No. 864 Beile Road; Ruichangxiang's cigarette and paper shop at No. 143 Avenue Edward VII; Zhu Liangchao's cigarette and paper shop at Shenjia浜, Avenue Foch (two robberies); Chen Changming's sock factory at No. 104 Renshou Lane, Caishi Road; Zhu Funian's rickshaw company at No. 340 Caishi Road; Cao Ruzhen's cigarette and paper shop at No. 147 Xiancheng Lane, Rue Pere Robert; Mi Lisen's cigarette and paper shop at No. 150 Rue du Pere Froc; Xu Yanggui's restaurant at No. 871 Avenue Joffre; Zhu Quanfa's house at No. 34 Meimu Lane, Avenue Joffre; and Zhang Xindi's inn on Avenue Edward VII. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, they were sent to the French Court for investigation. Judge Zhu Qi, together with French Consul Duge, sat in the criminal court. The Western police chief first reported the situation and presented the Mauser pistols and handgun for inspection. Then, the Chinese and Western detectives of the Putuo Road Police Station requested to move the interrogation. The plaintiffs also testified about the robberies. Chen Shuxing, Zhang Wu, and Chen Kaiqiang confessed to the robberies and the kidnapping. Xu and Zhang confessed that they were implicated by the others and did not dare to commit robberies, asking for leniency. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced Chen Shuxing, Zhang Wu, and Chen Kaiqiang to five years in the Western prison and deportation and sent them to the Mainland court for interrogation. They were first sent to the British Police Station for interrogation. The confiscated Mauser pistols were confiscated. Xu Xiaohuaizi and Zhang Jinlin were released without charge.

Lu Genbao's Death Was Due to Accidental Injury 160

▲Peng Shaobao May Be Subject to Leniency

Regarding the case reported on the 17th of this month about the death of rice boat crew member Lu Genbao from a gunshot wound, we have obtained further details and results, which are disclosed as follows. On February 16, a Jin-Hu ferry was docked at the Minnan wharf in Guanqiao. Several soldiers from the Songhu Garrison Command's reconnaissance team boarded the ferry to conduct an inspection. After the inspection was completed, one of the soldiers, Peng Shaobao, who was off duty, took out the bullets from his wooden-cased pistol on the deck of the ferry in preparation to return to the team. Suddenly, a bullet was discharged, accidentally hitting Lu Genbao, a crew member on the No. 4 rice boat moored next to the ferry, in the waist, causing his immediate death. The captain of the reconnaissance team rushed to the scene upon hearing the news and immediately took the soldier Peng Shaobao, who caused the accident, back for strict handling. He immediately notified the deceased's brother, Lu Genxiang, and repeatedly comforted him, offering generous compensation. The deceased's family believed that the incident was an accidental injury and were deeply grateful for the fair handling of the authorities. They have submitted a statement requesting that the soldier who caused the accident be treated leniently.

Recent Situation of Calligrapher and Painter Sun Xiaoting 167

Mr. Sun Xiaoting, a master of calligraphy and painting, has long been known in the art world. His seal engraving is based on the styles of the Qin and Han dynasties, and he does not follow contemporary trends. It is bold and simple, which is very admirable. His landscape paintings are based on the styles of Ni Zan, Wang Meng, Yun Shouping, and Wu Li, with clear and elegant brushstrokes, as if they have a magical quality. Last year, Mr. Sun donated seal engravings for three days, receiving a total of more than 30 pieces, which took two months to complete. It can be seen that there are many people who appreciate Mr. Sun's art. It is said that this spring, in order to continue his artistic pursuits, he will be accepting seal engravings at half price for five days starting from March 1st to gain the support of those who appreciate his art. Mountain and water paintings and outdated works will still be charged at the normal rate. Mr. Sun's residence is at No. 847, the intersection of Avenue Road and Matt Heath Road. Detailed price lists are available upon request.

The China Industrial Bank Establishes a Wuxi Branch 168

The China Industrial Bank in Shanghai has been expanding its business in recent years. In addition to the branches already established in various locations, it is now establishing a branch in Zhuchang Lane, Wuxi. It is scheduled to open on March 4. The president and vice president are Mr. Yuan Hongchao and Mr. Ye Youting, both of whom are talented individuals in the financial industry.

Nanjing Sock Factory Sells Off Its Remaining Stock 169

The Nanjing Sock and Shirt Factory at the north end of Zhejiang Road and Nanjing Road has been doing well since its opening. This spring, because the owner of the factory has no intention of continuing the business, he has decided to cease operations. It is now scheduled to start selling off the remaining stock from March 1st, regardless of cost, with the goal of selling everything off completely. It is also said that the shop's assets will also be sold at a low price.

"The Strange Man in the Old House" Will Be Shown at the Central Theater Starting Tomorrow 170

"The Strange Man in the Old House" is the latest production of the Shanghai Film Company. The plot is dreamlike and elusive. Hu Mingzhu plays a wealthy woman who possesses the key to a treasure cave, causing her to repeatedly encounter disasters. She is either trapped in a bandit's den or escapes barefoot into a broken boat. The dangerous situations are jaw-dropping. Her performance is even more remarkable than in her previous films. It is scheduled to be shown at the Central Theater for three days starting on March 1.

News from Trade Associations 171

▲The Biscuit and Candy Industry

The Biscuit, Candy, and Canned Goods Industry Association held a general meeting and a dinner, and elected Zhang Yichen as chairman. The following matters were reported: (1) The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter regarding the comparison of freight prices between domestic goods and similar foreign goods. It was resolved to reply to the Chamber of Commerce that the freight prices for various goods in this industry would be compared with those of foreign goods. (2) The Zhabei Defense Corps solicited donations for clothing. It was resolved to make a reasonable donation. (3) The Social Bureau issued an order to investigate the status of this industry. It was resolved to prepare a form and distribute it to each member for completion and submission. (4) Business tax proposal. It was resolved to send a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requesting that the situation of this industry be reduced to 2/1000 for tax collection and submitted to the authorities. (5) The Chinese Taxpayers' Association sent a letter requesting the recommendation of representatives. It was resolved to nominate Zhang Yichen and Le Fucheng as representatives of this association. (6) A proposal to encourage savings to create capital was adopted by the members. (7) Le Fucheng proposed that the customs tariff valuation for this industry was inconsistent. It was resolved to send a letter to each member requesting that they report the amount of tax paid to the association for discussion within a week. (8) Le Fucheng proposed that if there are arrears or uncleared accounts in the same industry, the association should be notified to inform the same industry to avoid more losses. The proposal was adopted. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

▲The Chicken and Duck Industry

The Chicken and Duck Industry Association sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce regarding the business tax issue, stating in brief: "Regarding the brokerage industry of our association, the draft of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Collection Regulations and Detailed Rules did not propose any method for collecting taxes from the brokerage industry. However, Article 2, Item 2 of the General Outline of Business Tax Collection Methods in various provinces and Article 13 of the Business Regulations in Anhui Province proposed methods for taxing the brokerage industry, although there are two methods: (1) determining the amount of tax to be collected and collecting 2/1000 of the brokerage fee, and (2) as a temporary measure, collecting the original brokerage tax. Although Zhejiang and Shanghai have not proposed such methods, they can be followed as examples to show the fairness of the legislation. Therefore, the business tax rate collected in our industry should be based on business income and the collection should be based on the brokerage fee, and should not be based on the fixed price of goods, which is obvious. We are responding to this letter, hoping that you will forward it to the authorities, and that the brokerage industry will collect taxes based on the brokerage fee and not exceed 2/1000."

Women's Circle Relief Leprosy Together 172

The Women's Support Association of the Chinese Leprosy Relief Association held its first annual meeting at Mrs. Guansen's residence yesterday (26th, 4:30 PM). The members were very enthusiastic. The meeting was chaired by Mrs. Zhang Jiafu, President, and Miss Li Caijingxiong reported. After the minutes of the previous meeting were read, Mrs. Bao was invited to speak on the responsibility of Christians to lepers. Her words were very pertinent. Then, Mr. Wu Zhijian, Secretary General of the General Association, reported on the daily work of the Association and its future plans. The meeting adjourned at dusk.

Autopsy of Chen Xianhua's Corpse 173

The suicide of dentist Chen Xianhua by taking nitric acid water has been reported. His body has been sent to the Philen Road autopsy room by the police. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo, commissioned by the Special District Local Court, arrived at the scene to clarify the matter and ordered the family members to sign a statement that the body had been placed in a coffin.

Letter Received

Respected Sir,

My neighbor, Jin Jun Shaohua, styled Baokang, childhood name Heshang, 26 years old, lives at No. 188, Qiaojia Road, inside the city of Nanshi. He works for the electricity bureau, earning a monthly salary of twenty or thirty yuan. He is usually honest and taciturn, going out early and returning late, walking instead of taking transportation, for several years. He has parents above him, and a wife, young son, and younger brother below him, who rely on him for their livelihood. Suddenly, on the 13th of this month (i.e., December 26th of the abandoned lunar calendar), he left for work in the morning and did not return at night. It has been half a month now, and there is no news of him. His family is extremely anxious, fearing that something bad has happened. They have reported to the Chinese Concession Police Bureau and the Life Saving Bureau, requesting them to pay attention and investigate. However, the six members of the Jin family will soon perish without his care. I intend to place a missing person ad in the newspaper, but I have no funds. Recognizing their suffering, I have taken the liberty of writing this letter, respectfully requesting that you publish this fact at the end of the newspaper. If kind-hearted gentlemen know of his whereabouts and are able to find him, not only will I be grateful beyond measure, but the Jin family will also be eternally grateful. Signed, Lu Jiayi.

P.S. Jin Jun is tall and thin, with a round, long, fair face. He wears a copper pot hat in snuff color, a tweed robe with a rabbit camel velvet lining, fingerless gloves in Shangqing color, old socks in snuff color, and black galoshes. He carries a black umbrella, one silver dollar, and more than ten copper coins.

We are writing to you regarding a case in which patrol officer Guo Wenjin brought three people, Tsukiji Jutarou and a young girl, and Sun Xiuting, to the Qiujiang Road, Alley 362 on the 22nd of this month due to a dispute. According to the investigation, the plaintiff stated that Tsukiji Jutarou, 50 years old, Japanese, a diver, had an argument with Sun Xiuting because Sun was playing with the young girl and spat on her face. Sun Xiuting, 34 years old, from Deng County, Shandong Province, a servant at No. 366, Qiujiang Road, stated that the Japanese girl knocked on my door, I opened the door and saw it was the young girl, we are familiar with each other, and I was playing with her and spat on her. Unexpectedly, she went home and told her parents that I hit her. So her parents and two others came to hit me. I didn't hit her. According to the investigation, Sun Xiuting, as a 34-year-old adult, should not be playing with a Japanese girl. Therefore, he was fined five yuan according to the police law. This is the course of the case. However, on February 24, the Shanghai Daily News reported that the wife of diver Tsukiji Jutarou was injured due to Sun Xiuting's violence and criticized our office for punishing the crime lightly. The director of our office was surprised when he read the report. Tsukiji Jutarou did not report that his wife was injured when he came to the office. If the injury was caused by violence and involved a criminal case, our office would have filed a lawsuit in court according to the law. If the injury required hospitalization, an injury certificate should have been presented when the case was filed, and our office would have handled it according to the law. Why didn't Tsukiji Jutarou report it at the time and only said that his daughter was bullied by Sun Xiuting and that he spat on her? On the 25th, the director of our office visited Japanese citizens Otsuki Shigeru and Kondo Hikaru because of the unresolved doubts. The two also mentioned the matter. They then went to Tsukiji Jutarou's residence to investigate. According to him, his wife's right ear was injured. When asked why he didn't report it that day, Tsukiji Jutarou said that he didn't understand the law of the Public Security Bureau at the time. It can be seen that our office punished the crime according to the situation and did not deal with it as a violation of police law because of the injury. Afterwards, our office summoned Sun Xiuting to the office again. Tsukiji Jutarou submitted a doctor's certificate from the hospital showing that his wife was injured. Our office immediately submitted it to the Public Security Bureau and sent a detailed letter to the Shanghai Daily News, but the newspaper has not corrected its mistakes or published the letter for three days. Therefore, we are sending this letter to the editor-in-chief, hoping that you will publish it in the news column.

Sincerely,

The First Division of the Fifth District of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau

Weather Report 175

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday was: The weather in the Yangtze River basin is cloudy, with some snowfall in some areas. There are northwest winds on the coast of Shandong. There are northwest winds south of Ma'an Island. Also, the highest temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 53.4 degrees and the lowest was 30.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 47.5 degrees and the lowest was 40.1 degrees.

Youth Garden

Enrollment 　Jiang Shanqing 176

Yesterday, my younger cousin, Heng, insisted on going to school. Mother couldn't keep her at home any longer. Although Mother knew she was ready for school, and that she genuinely wanted to go, she still pretended to object. I think this was a strategy, fearing that she would give up after only three days and find all sorts of excuses not to go. So she kept asking,

"Isn't it better if you don't go to school now? To avoid troubling me later and making me angry? It's fine if you don't go. If you do, you can't be lazy."

"Of course not, Mom. If I'm lazy, please hit me or scold me. I think, Mom, I definitely won't make you hit or scold me."

Finally, Mother agreed, giving her many more instructions. This morning, I took her to school to register. On the way, she was just happy, jumping and laughing constantly, one hand holding mine, the other clutching the empty schoolbag hanging on her shoulder. It was the one I used a couple of years ago, and Mother found it for her last night. Mother said,

"Taking advantage of your brother's success, you'll surely be smart enough to get top grades too."

When I arrived at school, I learned that fees were being collected today, and classes would start next Monday. I saw students crowding the accountant's window, some checking their receipts as they walked back.

I went to the school affairs office to complete Heng's enrollment procedures. I saw Principal Zou and other teachers, and I bowed to them respectfully.

"Zhang Yong, is this your sister? Did you bring her here to play?" Teacher Cheng put down his pen and asked me from his seat. "No, Teacher Cheng. She's here to register, preparing to enter the first grade."

"Excellent, how old is she?" Principal Zou asked.

"Six years old, Principal Zou."

"Take her to Teacher Qin to take a look, then let her in."

I took her to Teacher Qin, the first-grade teacher. She wrote a few words, "I am very happy to go to school today," and asked Heng to read them. Heng only recognized the word "feel." I knew she wouldn't be rejected. Teacher Qin was chatting with her to test her character and temperament, and also taught her to write and do simple arithmetic. I stood aside waiting. At this time, I listened to Principal Zou's words,

He drank half a glass of water, smoking a cigarette, and said to many teachers, "Now I am always very happy to see many students come here to study, and giving them more opportunity to study can wash away some of my sins."

"Some teachers know, I remember them talking about it, it was after the summer vacation two years ago when school started. A postman brought his son to register, requesting that we allow his son to transfer because his family had moved here, too far from the original school." "I looked at the report card, and the grades were not bad. Naturally, I wouldn't refuse them, but in fact, I couldn't. At that time, there were only seven classes here, and the classrooms were overcrowded. (Speaking, he pointed to the outside of the window) The buildings here hadn't been renovated yet. I checked, and there were already fifty-eight students in the third grade, and no matter what, I couldn't take him. The classroom definitely couldn't accommodate him. I said to him in a low voice, "The school has no reason to refuse any student's enrollment, especially students transferring within the city, but due to the city government's insufficient educational funding, the number of classes in each school has not been expanded as much as possible, which has resulted in an alarming number of out-of-school children throughout the city. Look, the third-grade classroom here is so crowded with desks and benches, and there's only one class, accommodating children who could be divided into two classes. Our school is extremely unwilling to refuse these out-of-school children, but in fact, we have had to refuse dozens of good children in the past few days. My heart as the principal is truly indescribably uncomfortable."

"Your school's situation is certainly understandable," the postman said, "My family's difficulties should also be understood. My family moved here to live so that I can work closer to the post office, but it is five or six li away from his original school. In any case, he can no longer go to school there. There is only this one school here, and the others are equally far away, so I ask you to find a way to let my child transfer here."

"I listened to him speaking earnestly, almost anxiously crying. His voice also changed. My heart was pricked like needles. I went to the third-grade classroom in person. I rearranged the desks and chairs, but in fact, I couldn't add another seat. I came back and told him, "According to the current situation, there is only this way. If you are willing to drop down a grade, he can attend the second grade, otherwise, wait until after the start of school to see if any third-grade students are absent due to circumstances, and then let him transfer here. What do you think?"

"He truly shed tears. He was indescribably aggrieved, perhaps regretting that he shouldn't have moved. He had to take the bewildered child away. Naturally, he was unwilling to let him drop down a grade. He came back once afterwards, and it happened that no third-grade students were absent. He finally left in disappointment."

"This matter often makes me ashamed, annoyed, and feel heartbroken. If this continues, can it still be considered the education of the glorious Republic of China? From this, I was like being stimulated, always thinking of negotiating with the authorities to expand our classes and accommodate more out-of-school children. This goal was finally achieved, with the renovation of these buildings and the addition of six grades of classrooms."

"So now, whenever I see new students arriving, I always feel indescribably happy, as if I can redeem my sins. I don't know how that student is now. If I had kept his name and address at the time, I would have found him first to study here."

He said a lot, and the cigarette in his hand burned to the end before he could smoke it. At this time, my cousin Heng had finished the test and was allowed to study in the first grade. I took her home, added the tuition for both of us, had lunch, and then went to the accountant's office to pay.

During these free days, it's good to review my vacation homework again.

Memorial Week for the Premier　Jiang Shanqing 177

Today is Monday, the first day of formal classes. At 8:30, the students gathered in the auditorium to hold the ceremony of the Memorial Week for the Premier, taking advantage of the morning assembly time.

I think the Memorial Week for the Premier is an active form of instruction, not idol worship, different from the prayers of Christians. When holding the Memorial Week for the Premier, recalling the past is far less important than encouraging the future or repenting of the present. The Premier's portrait hangs high under the shadow of the National Party flag, making you feel that he has not left this world. His spirit, his career, his personality, are entirely present before your eyes. If you have carefully and quietly experienced it, you can also feel that sacred inspiration, surging around you. He awakens your self-awareness, especially during the ceremony, making you eliminate pride, recognize your own insignificance, making you examine your achievements, and regret the negligence of effort. The prayers of Christians are nothing more than hope and blind following, emptiness and foolishness, so the two cannot be compared.

Even the lyrics of the "Premier Memorial Song" are significantly different in feeling, appreciation, and singing compared to flattering songs like "My Lord God."

Our Premier, first advocated revolution, revolutionary blood like flowers, overthrew autocracy, built the republic, produced my lord China,

The Republic of China is newly established, and state affairs are in a mess,

The Premier detailed plans, reforming China again,

X X X

The Three Principles of the People, the Five-Power Constitution, carefully pursuing the truth,

A lifetime of hardship, a lifetime of running around, struggling for national sacrifice,

The spirit of the Premier will last forever,

Like the Blue Sky with a White Sun, lasting for thousands of years,

X X X

The people's livelihood is declining, the country's steps are difficult, and the troubles have not yet ended. Do not disperse the group, do not lose heart, and encourage each other,

The Premier's last words, do not forget,

The revolution has not yet succeeded, and comrades still need to work hard,

These lyrics were distributed by the school, fearing that some people would not be able to sing them proficiently.

After singing the Party song and the Memorial Song for the Premier, the principal led the ceremony, respectfully reading the Premier's will and observing silence. When reciting the will, the voices were extremely neat and solemn, still like a collective awakened oath. During the silence, even the most mischievous students who liked to make funny faces were devout and quiet. The consciousness and emotions of four or five hundred people were all integrated. Today, at this moment, is when schools and organizations across the country are holding the Memorial Week for the Premier. On this clear morning, the consciousness and emotions of about tens of millions of people are also integrated. Tens of millions of people's minds are all remembering the Premier's spirit, career, and personality. They are all prepared, awakened, and encouraged to reproduce the Premier's spirit, emulate the Premier's personality, and strive to accomplish the Premier's unfinished career.

The principal and the dean of discipline both gave speeches. The principal also selectively reported on the recent Chinese political party affairs and the world situation. Because today is the first time to hold the Memorial Week for the Premier after the start of school, his more solemn words struck the listeners' hearts, leaving a deep impression. He further explained the significance of the Memorial Week for the Premier and the attitude we should have.

The Dean of Discipline followed with a fifteen-minute speech. He was the new Mr. Kong who was hired this semester. He also teaches us Party principles, history, and geography. He is very young, sincere, and stable. His speech is loud and clear, and his thinking is precise and correct. Everything about him can be my model. I think his teachings will leave me with a deep impression.

Today he explained the Premier's will, allowing me to begin to understand the essence it contains, and to pay attention to the three points of "must," "must," and "especially must."

It is necessary to awaken the masses, unite with the nations of the world that can treat me equally, and finally complete the Premier's forty-year purpose of seeking freedom and equality for China through revolution. Because if the masses cannot awaken, they cannot seek liberation themselves. If the nations that treat me equally cannot unite, they cannot defeat imperialism. Furthermore, without uniting with the weak and small nations of the world, the ideal of world harmony cannot be realized.

It is necessary to follow the Premier's theories and plans, strive to implement them, and finally have a correct direction and achieve the purpose of the revolution.

It is especially necessary to convene a national assembly in the shortest possible time, and finally build the foundation of constitutional government, abolish unequal treaties, and finally achieve the first step towards equality and freedom.

This will is indeed an instruction to the members of the Chinese Kuomintang, but since it is for the sake of the country's future, our people should have a clear understanding. Even at a young age, today's commemoration of the Premier is the first time in this semester, and because the students have gone through a long vacation, there is a warm emotion in the solemn gathering. This solemn warmth deeply moved me.

Manuscript Guidelines for Youth Corner 178

(1) The content should focus on discussions of youth issues, domestic and foreign studies, or student news, essays, descriptions of school life, random thoughts, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) Books are limited to those related to youth issues.
